The Ministry of Finance Advocates: No Ban on Wheat Exports; No Export Tax on Wheat Either 15

(Nanjing) The Baoding Chamber of Commerce and Shanghai merchant Gu Lugui previously telegraphed the Executive Yuan, stating that new wheat was entering the market and that foreigners were using capital to absorb it. They requested a ban on wheat exports or, when wheat was exported, the imposition of taxes based on import precedents to close loopholes. The Executive Yuan forwarded this to the Ministries of Finance and Industry for review. It is now learned that the Ministry of Finance believes that at the beginning of the new wheat season this year, Shanghai's foreign wheat prices fell. Later, due to poor wheat harvests in the United States and Canada, market prices soared, and China's wheat prices were also driven up. However, prices are still lower than when the new wheat entered the market. Regarding the issue of foreign merchants purchasing wheat in China, according to statistics from the National Tariff Commission, it is no more than 100,000 metric tons. Furthermore, the customs records show that the total amount of wheat exported in the first half of this year was 27,623 metric tons, which is a decrease compared to the same period last year. With a bountiful autumn harvest this year, allowing free circulation of domestic wheat should not affect people's livelihoods or hinder the flour industry. Furthermore, the customs has never banned wheat exports or taxed rice and wheat exports in the past, while taxing rice and wheat imports, to ensure the free circulation of domestic rice and wheat and prevent the dumping of foreign grain, so that farmers can receive real benefits. If a sudden ban on wheat exports or the imposition of export taxes were implemented when wheat prices are slightly higher and there are a few foreign shipments, it would seem to contradict the government's original intention of protecting the rural economy. Moreover, the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Association has petitioned the government for relief, stating that wheat is stockpiling and congesting the market, and if exports are not urgently promoted, it will harm rural areas and hinder finance. This shows that merchants have different viewpoints due to their different positions. If wheat exports are banned, it is feared that disputes will arise. As a result of the Ministry's review, it does not support approving the requests of the Baoding Chamber of Commerce and Gu Lugui and has submitted this to the Executive Yuan for review. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 17th)

Miscellaneous News on the National Election 16

(Nanjing) The National Election Headquarters recently clarified the doubts raised by various parties regarding the invalidation of ballots: (1) If the name written on the ballot does not match the name recorded in the citizen register or the register of officials and members, but it can be proven that it is definitely the same person, it should be considered valid. (2) If the name or alias of the nominee is inconsistent, such as one ballot writing the name and another ballot writing the alias, if it can be proven that it is definitely the same person, the ballot writing the alias should also be considered valid. (3) Common writing styles, such as writing the "欠" radical of "漱" as "文," and (4) abbreviated writing styles, such as writing "萬" as "万," "陞" as "升," and "齋" as "垒," should all be considered valid. (5) The nominee's place of origin should be noted on the nomination ballot, as explicitly stipulated in the first section of Article 6 of the Implementing Regulations for the Election Law. Therefore, if the nominee's place of origin is not filled in, the nominee is invalid. (6) If the number of nominees recorded on the ballot exceeds the legal limit, they should be counted in order, and those exceeding the limit are invalid, but those within the limit are valid. (7) If the nomination ballot has the nominee's nickname, (8) if the names of the nominees written are homophones with different characters, (9) if the candidate has already changed their name, but the nominator still writes their original name, the above three points, if it can be accurately proven that they all refer to the same person, and there is no conflict with the headquarters' established standards for invalid ballots, the nomination ballot should be considered valid. However, it is more difficult to prove whether homophones with different characters refer to the same person, so it should be handled with particular caution. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 17th)

(Nanjing) The Election Office for Representatives of the Four Provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe previously sent a letter to the National Election Headquarters regarding whether a citizen with more than two types of special election qualifications could be allowed to choose. The headquarters answered that, upon investigation, those with more than two special election rights are the same as those with more than two election rights in occupational elections and can be handled in the same way. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 17th)

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Regional Election still lacks four candidates. A supplementary election was held in the City Hall auditorium at 9:00 am on the 17th, and Sun Quanzhang and four others were elected. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 17th)

All postage stamps with the words "Limited to Use in Sichuan" printed on them will be discontinued, and those that have not yet been used up will be allowed to be used at various post offices in Sichuan Province when mailing letters and packages until the end of March of the 26th year. If there are any remaining at that time, they will be allowed to be exchanged for ordinary postage stamps at various post offices in Sichuan Province within three months; they will be invalid after the deadline. Page 7

Stimson Disclosed the Principles of US Policy Towards China; Fulfilling Treaty Obligations and Maintaining Friendship; China's Future Must Develop on Its Own 38

(New York) The book "The Far Eastern Crisis: Recollections and Observations" by former US Secretary of State Stimson will be published today by the Council on Foreign Relations. China occupies an important place in the book, and Stimson describes the basic principles of US policy during Japan's invasion of Manchuria as follows:

(1) Fulfill all treaty obligations to maintain future friendly relations between China and the United States.

(2) Safeguard the foundation of cooperative action to maintain world peace. According to Stimson, the above two principles are often criticized as having exceeded the usual course of diplomatic action. Stimson said, "I am prepared to deal with this kind of criticism. Even in peacetime, a foreign minister cannot allow his vision to be obscured by temporary events. But as it is today, new developments occur almost daily, which may have a significant impact on the future, and the danger of taking a narrow view of the entire purpose is greatly increased."

Stimson's book also states about China: "The future of China is a major issue of the times. One thing is quite clear, that China must develop on its own and cannot be controlled or driven by foreign forces, making it an unwanted evolution from the outside. China has the world's oldest culture and 4,000 years of history to prove it. The peaceful nature of China's internal culture is the main stabilizing element in Asia today. The loss of this element in China will directly affect the peace of its neighbors, including the United States. If this loss is caused by the United States disregarding its treaty obligations, then this policy is too short-sighted. Some Americans believe that to solve the Manchuria problem, the United States and Japan must agree on a solution that benefits Japan. They have forgotten that the Manchuria problem is China's most important fundamental problem. Any agreement or solution that Japan agrees to at present will be seen by China as destructive and rejected."

Stimson also discussed the efforts of cooperation between the United States and Britain, saying that in February 1932, as the world situation became increasingly dark, he consulted with President Hoover and proposed to the British Ambassador to the United States that the United States and Britain jointly fulfill their obligations under the Nine-Power Treaty to stop Japan's actions. A few days later, Stimson also spoke with British Foreign Secretary Sir John Simon over the transatlantic wireless telephone and urged him to agree. Stimson also said, "I further discussed this matter with Sir John Simon in London on February 13th and 15th. Although Simon did not explicitly reject my proposal, it was clear from his attitude that the British government was unwilling to join, so I did not urge it further."

Therefore, Stimson wrote to Senator Borah, reiterating the US insistence on the non-recognition policy. Stimson went on to describe the necessity of future cooperation between the United States and Britain, saying, "I have earnestly explained our experience of cooperation with the British government and believe that the ultimate development of European collective action, whether through the current League of Nations or by other means, the great responsibility of leadership will inevitably be borne by the British government and its dominions. This is unavoidable. I believe that this responsibility of leadership should not be hindered by the fear that collective action will be obstructed by non-League members such as the US government. This is the most important way to guarantee this security and the cooperation of the two governments. All executive steps that occupy an important part in international action must be sincere, effective, and traditional." (Reuters dispatch from the 17th)

Soviet Russian Defense Commissioner Warns Western Powerful Enemies: Not Allowed to Covet an Inch of Russian Territory; Anyone Who Dares to Attack Will Surely Be Defeated 39

(Moscow) On the 14th of this month, People's Commissar of Defense Marshal Voroshilov inspected the training troops of the Kiev Military District and delivered a speech praising the order and organization of the exercise as excellent. He also expressed his gratitude to the workers and collective farmers for their help and care for the Red Army. The next day, the troops held a grand parade. Voroshilov delivered another speech congratulating the soldiers, commanders, and political commissar Yagil. After the speeches, the troops held a grand parade lasting two hours. (TASS dispatch on the 16th)

(Moscow) Soviet Defense Commissioner Voroshilov arrived in Zhitomir on the 16th, where he was warmly welcomed by local party and government leaders and 150,000 people. The whole city was extremely lively. The people held a welcome rally in the square in front of the station. Representatives of the workers delivered welcoming speeches, mentioning their happy lives and progress in culture and economy, as well as their determination to rise up at any time to defend the socialist motherland.

Voroshilov then gave a reply, representing the Central Party Department and the government to congratulate all the workers of Ukraine. He continued, "You have expressed to me on behalf of the Party and the government that the workers of the whole of Ukraine and its capital will be an unshakable vanguard of our socialist motherland. The Soviet Union has many enemies. They are trying to turn our socialist country into a field of rubble, and our workers into the slaves of nineteen years ago. But the enemies are completely wrong. They do not know the strength and consolidation of the Soviet Union. They do not know that the collective cooperation of our 170 million people has made extraordinary achievements in all aspects of socialist construction. They can move forward on a new path of life, eliminating any obstacles from the enemy. We must bear in mind the lessons of Lenin and Stalin. We must be prepared at any time to build socialism while not forgetting to defend socialism. This lesson has been accepted by all our workers. They are strengthening national defense while building, and are inextricably linked with the strong worker-peasant Red Army. "Our Red Army is you. We are not only your blood and flesh, but also your spirit, thoughts, expectations, and hopes. We can swear to you that our Red Army worker-peasant soldiers will never fail your expectations and will never make you uneasy. The people of Kiev know well the actions that the enemies of the workers can take. In the past three years, Kiev has been occupied fifteen times by different enemies, transferred from the hands of one despicable enemy to another. The working men and women of Kiev can remember the madness of the capitalists, the barbarity, cruelty, stupidity, and rudeness shown in this city. You can remember the past, but the past will never come again. Although some gentlemen are dreaming of setting foot on Soviet territory, they will never succeed. Our government. Our Party. Our great Stalin himself has repeatedly declared sincerely to the world that our country is a country of peace, a country that can guarantee peace throughout the world. Our country was the first to propose disarmament. Although we dearly love our Red Army and are deeply proud of its organization, combat effectiveness, weapons, and good condition, we are still willing to disband this Red Army without hesitation and send it to factories and collective farms if capitalist countries accept our disarmament proposal. But our class enemies cannot accept it. They are not entirely because they fear us. They claim that we are red warlords and that our Red Army is preparing to attack, which is a deliberate lie. They do not want disarmament because they fear their own people and their own workers. Our country is a peaceful country. Our Red Army is not only our country's most willing to do its best to guarantee peace in the world. If we cannot succeed in this regard, it is not our fault. If any enemy attempts to attack our country and force all our workers, peasants, intellectuals, and the men and women of our country to stop building great socialist buildings and mobilize arms, then comrades, we are ready to fight them (thunderous applause). I have just returned. I saw the large-scale exercises in the Belorussian Military District and the tactical exercises in the Kiev District of Sheptovka. These two exercises have shown that our Red Army has grown as much as our workers and peasants. We have not saved a single day of eating Soviet bread. We have made great progress in the past year. We have "jumped" from junior high school or high school to university (applause). I can assure all the workers of Ukraine that whenever our enemy launches a mad attack, our Red Army will be able to resist it with all its strength. I have stated repeatedly, and I now repeat it to the whole of Ukraine, that we have only one wish, that is, if the enemy attacks Ukraine, Belarus, or any part of the Soviet Union, we will not only not let the enemy enter our motherland by one step, but will defeat them in the place from which they came (applause and cheers). This statement does not conflict with my previous statement that our Red Army and country are still the guarantee of peace. The current war will be extremely brutal and terrible because it possesses vicious weapons that the world has never seen or heard of before. In this way, you can imagine how unimaginable the destruction would be if the battle took place on our territory. Therefore, we must prepare a method, and not only the worker-peasant Red Army but even all of you workers, must be prepared in advance. If the enemy appears, they must be defeated immediately in their own territory (applause and cheers), and they must be severely injured so that after receiving a lesson, they will never dream of turning our workers and collective farmers into slaves. We should be excellent teachers, Bolshevik teachers, and use this method to teach those gentlemen so that if they can survive to that time, they will warn their great-grandchildren never to attack the Soviet state again (applause). A ten-day air defense exercise is currently being held here, which is the best thing. I congratulate all the participating comrades. This kind of air defense exercise should be held not only by a certain person, not only by this beautiful and glorious Kiev, but by all places in the country where people live. At present, aviation, especially high-speed aviation, can reach any place at any time, even our vast motherland. For this reason, you must organize truly reliable air defense, so that in this beautiful city of Kiev, all weapons have appropriate defense methods. Aviation is not omnipotent. If the air defense is organized properly, aviation cannot cause great damage, and our city has not only anti-aircraft guns, but also a glorious air force and heroic and outstanding aviators. Comrades, I thank you for your welcome and congratulations. I accept it on behalf of the worker-peasant Red Army and will convey it to our Central Party Department and government, as well as to our great Stalin. I will tell Stalin that not only his capital Kiev, but even the workers of the entire Ukraine, have become a truly outstanding Soviet collective. They not only work in the Stakhanov method, but are also the pioneers and organizers of the Stakhanov socialist construction method, and at the same time, they are a collective that can join the ranks of the worker-peasant Red Army at any time and rise up to defend their great socialist motherland." (Tidal wave of applause and cheers, lasting for a long time. (TASS dispatch on the 17th)

(Moscow) The Soviet Russian authorities are promoting a policy of building roads with convict labor. They are now rushing to build two military motor roads to the Polish border to cope with the Western border war crisis. There are now thousands of convicts working in shifts of 24 hours to rush the construction. At night, the lights illuminate the area like daylight. The roads currently under construction are the eastern sections of the main roads to Minsk and Kiev, and are expected to be completed by November 7. The Soviet Russian authorities do not admit that these roads have military value, but the progress of their construction is obviously faster than the construction of other important roads. Minsk and Kiev are both important towns in Soviet Russia. (National Electric dispatch on the 16th)

US Forms European Fleet, Claiming It Is of a Temporary Nature 40

(Washington) The Navy Department announced today that the United States has organized a "temporary" European fleet under the command of Rear Admiral Van Vleet. The flagship of the fleet is the light cruiser Raleigh, followed by the destroyers Gaines, Hatfield, and the Coast Guard cutter Cayuga. The fleet will be officially established as soon as the Raleigh arrives in Gibraltar. The United States has long abandoned the European fleet since 1929 in order to save money. (National Electric dispatch on the 16th)

(Washington) The Navy Department recently announced that the United States government has decided to form a fleet and order it to be temporarily stationed in European waters, consisting of the light cruiser Raleigh, the destroyers Hatfield, Caine, and the communication ship Cayuga, and to appoint Vice Admiral Fairfield as the commander. The US Navy originally had a fleet stationed in European waters, which was later withdrawn. Now, due to the tense situation in Europe, it has been reorganized. (Havas dispatch on the 16th)

New League of Nations Building Completed; General Assembly to Open Next Monday; China Proposes to Strengthen the Covenant; League of Nations Council to Meet in New Building Today; Abyssinian Attendance Issue to Cause Dispute 41

(Geneva) It is expected that when the League of Nations General Assembly opens next Monday, it will be proposed to elect China as a member of the League of Nations Council and ask the House to pass it. The new League of Nations building, costing one million pounds, has recently been completed. The Council will hold its first meeting there tomorrow, but because the decoration of the General Assembly hall has not been completed, the Council meeting will be held on the third floor of the building. The Chinese Ambassador to the United Kingdom, Guo Taiqi, will arrive here tomorrow. (Reuters dispatch on the 17th)

(Geneva) The Secretariat of the League of Nations, in accordance with the resolution passed by the extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations General Assembly in July, solicited the opinions of the member states on the amendment of the Covenant. The Chinese government recently sent a proposal to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, advocating that the Covenant of the League of Nations, especially Article 11 of the Covenant, which contains measures to prevent war, should be strengthened as much as possible, and the definition of the aggressor should also be clearly defined. Regarding measures to prevent war, the Chinese government believes that this can be implemented without the approval of all members of the Executive Council. Regarding the various sanction measures contained in Article 16 of the Covenant, it advocates the establishment of a permanent committee of experts to formulate long-term and effective provisions so that the sanction measures can be "automatically, immediately, and fully implemented." In addition, it also suggests the establishment of a special committee to decide in advance on the military sanction measures to be taken in an emergency. As for the conclusion of regional security treaties, the Chinese government is willing to accept its principles, but only if this treaty does not go beyond the scope of the Covenant. (Havas dispatch on the 17th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations General Assembly will hold an important meeting next Monday. Now that the exiled Emperor of Abyssinia has decided to send a representative to attend, an abnormal situation seems to be arising. It is widely speculated that the Credentials Committee will refuse to recognize the existence of any independent government in Abyssinia. Therefore, whether the Emperor of Abyssinia is still qualified to send a representative to attend the League of Nations General Assembly has become a question. It is also expected that the Italian request to represent Abyssinia will be ignored by the League of Nations. Mr. Lammass, the Foreign Minister of Argentina, has the best chance of being elected as the chairman of this General Assembly. Mr. Lammass has always advocated not recognizing the fruits of aggression, so his position seems to be difficult. As for the United Kingdom, it will send a powerful delegation to the General Assembly. Foreign Secretary Eden, who recently recovered from chickenpox, will be the head of the delegation. Other representatives are the Lord Privy Seal and Leader of the House of Lords, Viscount Halifax, Foreign Under-Secretary Cranborne, and Dominion Secretary Malcolm MacDonald. (Reuters dispatch on the 17th)

(Geneva) The Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, received a note from the Emperor of Abyssinia this morning, stating that he has appointed Walkerner and Sheesh as representatives of his country to attend the current League of Nations General Assembly. (Havas dispatch on the 17th)

(London) The Emperor of Abyssinia recently made a statement in Amharic to our correspondent, saying, "Whether I will go to Geneva when the League of Nations General Assembly opens is still undecided. I will make a decision after the report of our delegation is submitted. If necessary, I plan to preside over it personally. As for our delegation, it was originally formed in accordance with the law. The League of Nations has no other attitude to take except to recognize the rights it should enjoy." He also said that the government of Gore in western Abyssinia does not have enough arms for self-defense and should purchase them from foreign countries, but he has not yet requested the British government to allow travelers and goods from his country to pass through the British territory of East Africa, and it is not yet known whether the French government will allow them to pass through the territory of France due to the tense situation in Europe. (London) The Abyssinian Embassy in the United Kingdom announced today that the Abyssinian Ambassador to the United Kingdom, Dr. Martin, will go to Geneva to attend the annual General Assembly of the League of Nations. As for whether the Emperor of Abyssinia is preparing to attend Geneva personally, according to Abyssinian sources here, no decision has been made yet, but it is said that the local leaders who are continuing to resist in western Abyssinia are still maintaining regular contact with the Emperor. The general public in the United Kingdom is quite concerned about the decision of Abyssinia to send a representative to Geneva, and it is not known what attitude the British delegation will take on the issue of recognizing the qualifications of the Abyssinian representative to attend the League of Nations. It is up to the Credentials Committee of the General Assembly to decide whether the Abyssinian representative can participate in the work of the League of Nations General Assembly. However, some left-wing figures believe that if the Abyssinian delegation can attend Geneva, it will make Italy take a more accommodating attitude towards participating in the Locarno Five-Power Conference. What Italy hopes is that the Abyssinian affair should be completely settled in the international arena after the Abyssinian affair. In fact, the Italian war in Abyssinia has not ended, and Italy is still far from completely controlling Abyssinia. If Italy is too hasty in Geneva, it will instead unite other countries against the settlement of the Abyssinian affair. This should also be a concern for Italy. (Havas dispatch on the 16th)

(Geneva) The Abyssinian Embassy in the United Kingdom announced today that the Emperor of Abyssinia has decided to send a delegation to represent Abyssinia at the League of Nations General Assembly. The League of Nations may receive formal notification of this matter tomorrow. According to international sources, the League of Nations may raise some questions about the validity of the credentials of the Abyssinian delegation, thereby preventing the Abyssinian delegation from participating in the work of the General Assembly. (Havas dispatch on the 16th)

(Rome) Political figures here unanimously believe that the Abyssinian decision to send a representative to Geneva will result in Italy not attending the League of Nations General Assembly. According to responsible sources, although the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, came to Rome some time ago to consult with the Italian government, the Italian government has not taken any binding measures on the issue of Italian cooperation with Geneva. Therefore, whether Italy will attend the League of Nations General Assembly will depend on the final situation. Even if the credentials of the Abyssinian delegation are deemed invalid by the League of Nations General Assembly, if the Abyssinian delegation is already in Geneva, the Italian delegation will inevitably delay attending the League of Nations General Assembly, because the fascist government must obtain guarantees so that the Italian representative will not meet the Abyssinian representative in Geneva before it can send a representative to attend the League of Nations General Assembly. (Havas dispatch on the 16th)

(Paris) With the League of Nations General Assembly and Executive Council about to open, the French delegation has been officially announced, consisting of Foreign Minister Delbos, former Minister without Portfolio Peng Gu, and Minister of Economy Steinas as the main representatives, and Minister of Commerce Bassette and Chairman of the Senate Foreign Affairs Committee Bellanger as the deputy representatives. As for the attitude that the delegation should adopt at the League of Nations, it will be determined after the Foreign Minister has consulted with friendly countries, especially the representatives of certain countries in the Little Entente. But in general, there are several items: (1) France will discuss various economic issues at length. This can be seen from the fact that Minister of Economy Spinasse and Minister of Commerce Basset are attending the League of Nations. In addition, the League of Nations Economic Committee, which met on the 9th of this month, also advocated convening an international economic and tariff conference, which is welcome to France. (2) Since the French Parliament recently voted to add funds to improve military equipment, the government intends to launch an initiative to stop the arms race, and the French delegation should follow this principle and make proposals. (3) Regarding the issue of strengthening the League of Nations Covenant, the French delegation already expressed its attitude at the extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations General Assembly at the end of June, and should continue to do so. (4) The French delegation should join the British delegation to contact the Portuguese Foreign Minister Monteiro again and urge Portugal to send a representative to participate in the Non-Intervention Committee for the Spanish Civil War. Other issues such as the Free City of Danzig and the Abyssinian issue have become secondary matters and can be discussed at leisure, especially since the Emperor of Abyssinia's decision to send a representative to the General Assembly has raised procedural issues, and the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, may make a proposal. (Havas dispatch on the 17th)

World Radio Conference to Negotiate International Convention; Use Radio to Promote Peace 44

(Geneva) The World Radio Conference opened here today. All League of Nations member states and major non-League of Nations member states were invited to participate in the meeting. The purpose of the meeting is to draft a world convention to use radio to promote world peace. The signatory countries will be responsible for preventing the broadcasting of radio sounds that incite the people of other countries to engage in war within their borders, and will guarantee the accuracy of the broadcast of international affairs news. Of the 40 countries concerned, 19 have now accepted this agreement, and 11 more, including the United Kingdom, plan to accept it with certain conditions. The United States has refused to join the agreement because radio broadcasting is not under government jurisdiction. (Reuters dispatch on the 17th)

Spanish Government Forces Destroy the Alcázar of Toledo; Two Armies in Contact at Oropesa 45

Madrid: Government forces bombarded the Alcázar of Toledo all day today. By the time the bombardment ceased, this historically famous fortress was nothing but ashes. The 1,200 soldiers, women, and children inside were likely buried in the rubble. (16th National Telegram)

Madrid: The government today issued an emergency decree to recruit 10,000 volunteer troops to begin military training, so that they may immediately go to the front lines to fight. These volunteers will largely go to Talavera, preparing for a counter-offensive against the rebels. (17th National Telegram)

San Sebastián: The rebel forces previously announced a temporary halt, but today have resumed their eastward advance. At the same time, the naval blockade of the ports of Santander and Bilbao has also begun. Rebel troops, with Moorish soldiers as their vanguard, forced the government outposts at Oropesa to retreat 13.5 miles westward and defend Jaraz. The rebel forces have now occupied Oropesa and the nearby areas of Alcañizo and Espinoso del Rey. Whether this advance is a solitary action by the troops there, or whether the rest period has been shortened, is not stated. Meanwhile, the Burgos government has issued a public notice warning the world that it will blockade Bilbao and Santander, lest anyone claim ignorance and cause unforeseen incidents. (16th National Telegram)

Hendaye: A special dispatch from our agency states that government forces and rebel forces came into contact in the city of Oropesa last night. Government militiamen destroyed bridges, cutting off the rebels' communications with the outside world, causing great difficulty. They were forced to flee into the surrounding mountains of Oropesa to resist. The situation in Santoña is also very tense. Anarchists have occupied all public buildings in the city, taking on guard duties and trying opponents, and arrested a Socialist member of parliament and imprisoned him. (16th Havas Telegram)

Burgos: A special dispatch from our agency's correspondent states that the National Guard in the besieged city of Oviedo in the northwest launched a surprise counterattack yesterday and repelled a column of government troops. The column led by National Guard General Teijeiro is rapidly advancing towards the city, having advanced 20 kilometers in half a month and seized several villages and towns. (17th Havas Telegram)

Hendaye: According to indirect reports from here, the anarchists in Santander, a town 47 miles northwest of Bilbao in northern Spain, now control everything. The police and judiciary are entirely under their control, and the situation is precarious. One Socialist member of parliament has been arrested, and another has fled the area. Anarchists and members of the Popular Front are reportedly engaging in nightly gun battles. Note that Santander is a sheltered harbor in the Bay of Biscay, with a resident archbishop and a 13th-century ancient church in the town. (17th Reuters Telegram)

Madrid: Foreign Minister Del Vayo is scheduled to depart for Geneva today to attend the League of Nations Council and the regular session of the General Assembly. Yesterday, he made a statement to the press, saying, "There is no doubt that the government will win in its suppression of the rebels. This conflict is not merely a domestic event in Spain, but indeed a European event. In short, the entire peace of Europe has been affected. The Spanish government firmly believes that all those who seek to maintain world peace will certainly provide full assistance to the Spanish government in its suppression of the rebellion." (17th Havas Telegram)

French Labor Strike; Labor and Management Reach Compromise; Mediation by the Prime Minister 47

(Paris) Regarding the mediation of the textile workers' strike in Lille, negotiations have continued since this morning, and labor and management have virtually reached a compromise on the wage issue. It is expected that the first protocol will be signed this afternoon. The purpose of the negotiations between the two sides is twofold: one is to determine the method of electing worker representatives, and the other is to discuss the issue of wage increases. Regarding the former, i.e., the issue of worker representatives, although labor representatives made some concessions this morning, their opinions still differ greatly from those of the management, and there is no hope of a compromise. Therefore, the government representatives decided to discuss the wage issue, and as a result, the management representatives agreed to re-regulate wages in accordance with the current wage levels in other textile regions. (17th Havas Telegram)

(Paris) Regarding the textile workers' strike in Lille, Prime Minister Léon Blum summoned representatives from both labor and management today to continue mediation. From 5:00 PM today, representatives from the government, employers, and employees held a meeting at the prefecture of the Nord department for negotiations. Those attending on behalf of the government were Prime Minister Léon Blum, Minister without Portfolio Jouhaux, and Interior Minister Salengro. The delegation of textile employers in Lille was led by Thilliez, President of the Textile Industry Association, and the delegation of employees was led by Dumoulin, Secretary of the Nord Department Labor Union. At 9:45 PM, the Interior Minister told the press, "We have met with the employer and employee delegations successively, and have now met with the employer delegation for the second time. The talks are largely over. From now on, labor and management representatives can negotiate together. The point of contention between the two sides lies entirely in the wage issue." At 10:00 PM, the employers held their own meeting for discussion, and at 11:10 PM, they left the prefecture. The employee delegation then also withdrew, and Dumoulin told the press that the workers hoped to negotiate face-to-face with the employers tomorrow, but "this is only a hope." As for whether the two sides can reach an agreement, it will be known after the government solicits 20,000 opinions. Subsequently, government ministers also left the prefecture, but did not issue a statement. As it stands, although negotiations are still underway, they will not be resolved tonight. It is reported that the workers previously demanded a 20% wage increase, but have now retreated to 10%. Whether the employers can accept this is still unknown. (16th Havas Telegram)

(Paris) Regarding the mediation of the textile workers' strike in Lille, negotiations resumed at 9:30 AM this morning. The labor representatives were received by Minister without Portfolio Jouhaux, and the management representatives were received by Interior Minister Salengro, but Prime Minister Léon Blum did not participate. Thilliez, the leader of the management delegation, told the press, "This dispute is actually about the struggle for authority. The striking workers occupy factories and offices, and at the same time hold demonstrations, all of which are detrimental to our authority, status, and independence. These three are indispensable for managing factories. In short, the management has two preconditions before discussing the wage increase issue: (1) Workers are not allowed to occupy factories and offices again in the future; (2) The method of electing worker representatives and their rights and obligations must be stipulated, so that the employer's authority can be fully maintained." (17th Havas Telegram)

Copenhagen: Chinese Minister to Denmark Luo Zhongyi, who has served for ten years, returned home with his family yesterday. A large crowd came to see them off. Securities

American businessman Robertson stated that general commerce has reached the greatest period in American history. Those in the market who had adopted a wait-and-see attitude were encouraged by this. Commercial news continues to be trustworthy. French North and South Pole Exploration Ship Sinks off the Coast of Iceland; Only One Survivor 50

Copenhagen: According to a wireless message from Scoresby Sund, Greenland, the French Arctic exploration ship "Pourquoi-Pas?" sank in a storm off the coast of Iceland. All crew members except one perished, totaling 30 victims. The captain of the expedition, the famous North and South Pole explorer Charcot, was also among them. All bodies were washed away by the waves and could not be recovered. Details are still unknown. The discovery was made by the Danish Navy patrol ship "Thetis." The ship, departing from the capital of Iceland, was patrolling the waters of Straumnesfjord, not far from the location of the "Pourquoi-Pas?" disaster. They saw a broken ship's mast sticking out of the sea, so they approached to investigate, and discovered that it was the French exploration ship "Pourquoi-Pas?". No one was climbing on the top of the mast, indicating that all crew members had perished. Only one person survived. He drifted at sea holding a piece of wood from the ship and eventually reached the shore. At that time, he was unconscious and was carried on a stretcher to a nearby farmhouse. After drinking coffee, he regained consciousness slightly, and then immediately fell asleep. He has not yet awakened, so his name and the details of the disaster are currently impossible to ascertain. (16th Havas Telegram)

Copenhagen: Regarding the sinking of the French Arctic exploration ship "Pourquoi-Pas?" off the coast of Iceland, it is now known that the disaster site was indeed in Straumsfjord. Twenty-one bodies of the crew members have washed up on the coast, including the body of the captain, the famous North and South Pole explorer Dr. Charcot. Only one of the crew members survived, the boatswain, named Guidet. He is now awake. According to him, when the ship sailed to Reykjanes Point, it was suddenly hit by a giant storm from the southwest. They immediately turned the rudder to retreat, but lost their way. Until 5:30 AM yesterday morning, it ran aground on a reef. At that time, the sea was stormy, and there was no time to launch the lifeboats. The deck was immediately flooded, and the boiler exploded. The French consul here stated that the ship had a total of 40 crew members. (17th Havas Telegram)

Saint-Malo: The Arctic Ocean exploration ship "Pourquoi-Pas?", which sank in the Icelandic waters, was registered in the French port of Saint-Malo. The owner and captain was the famous explorer Dr. Charcot. The ship was built in 1908. It was a wooden motorboat, equipped with sails, 140 meters long, 31 meters wide, and 15 meters deep. The ship left the port of Saint-Servan near here on June 22, via Sweden, carrying one member of the Swedish exploration team, and then sailed to the Greenland area to conduct scientific research. Afterward, the ship was originally scheduled to sail to Scoresby Sund to meet with members of the French exploration team who landed there in 1935, but unexpectedly encountered danger and sank on the way. (16th Havas Telegram)

(Paris) The academic community is deeply saddened by the news of the sinking of the famous French North and South Pole explorer Dr. Charcot, along with his famous exploration ship "Pourquoi-Pas?", in the waters near Iceland. Dr. Charcot was born in 1867 in Neuilly-sur-Seine. His father was a doctor, and Charcot initially followed his father's profession as a doctor, but later became known as an "explorer." The exploration ships he captained were initially the "Français" and later the "Pourquoi-Pas?". From 1903 to 1905 and from 1908 to 1910, he went to Antarctica twice to conduct oceanographic research and map the Antarctic continent completely, thus gaining fame. Later, a place on the Antarctic continent was named after Charcot. Afterward, Charcot conducted several explorations in the North Atlantic. His explorations were compiled into several volumes, including "Voyage to Antarctica" and "The Pourquoi-Pas? Expedition." Despite being in his seventies, he never ceased to travel to the far seas for exploration. Charcot served successively as the Director of the Oceanographic Institute, a researcher at the Hydrographic Office, and a member of the Marine Academy. In 1921, he was elected to the Academy of Sciences, and in 1930, he was elected to the Academy of Medicine. He also received medals and awards from the French and foreign governments. He is survived by his wife and two daughters. (16th Havas Telegram)

Average Index of Rural Land Prices in Various Provinces in the Last Five Years 61

(Nanjing) The Central Agricultural Experiment Station has announced the average index of rural land prices in various provinces of our country for the past five years. The calculation is as follows: 100 for paddy fields in 1931, 100 for flat land, and 100 for mountainous land; 95 for paddy fields in 1932, 93 for flat land, and 94 for mountainous land; 89 for paddy fields in 1933, 87 for flat land, and 88 for mountainous land; 82 for paddy fields in 1934, 83 for flat land, and 82 for mountainous land; 81 for paddy fields in 1935, 83 for flat land, and 82 for mountainous land. According to the station's observation of the above figures, land prices have been declining year by year since 1931, and only began to stabilize in 1935. However, compared with 1931, they are still about 18% lower. The reason for this is that there have been frequent droughts and floods in the past five years, and the Communist bandits have been causing trouble, so there has been a great downward trend. Now that domestic politics are gradually becoming stable, the Communist bandits have been largely eliminated, and farmers have been able to live and work in peace. In the future, rural land prices will naturally tend to rebound. (Central News Agency dispatch, 17th)

Education Broadcasting Special Issue

How to Promote Rural Sideline Occupations (Part 1) 68

— Qian Tianhe, Deputy Director of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station

1. What are Rural Sideline Occupations?

Before explaining what rural sideline occupations are, let's first talk about what we call sideline occupations. Sideline occupations themselves do not have a fixed standard, but are relative terms to principal occupations. Generally speaking, it refers to engaging in a certain occupation as the central enterprise for one's livelihood, and then using the remaining time and labor to engage in other occupations to increase income and supplement the insufficiency of one's central enterprise. These other occupations are sideline occupations, and the central enterprise for one's livelihood is the principal occupation. For example, a plasterer usually works when there is work, and pulls a rickshaw when there is no work. Pulling a rickshaw is a sideline occupation, and working as a plasterer is the principal occupation. Another example is a bank clerk who usually serves and works in the bank, which is the principal occupation, but in his spare time, he grows some vegetables and horticulture, and after his family enjoys them, he sells the rest to the market to get some profit, which is a sideline occupation.

The so-called rural sideline occupations mean that the central enterprise for one's livelihood must be agriculture, and the people engaged in it must be farmers. Farmers, in addition to engaging in their central enterprise for their livelihood, use their remaining time and labor, or use vacant land and residual materials, or process and manufacture agricultural products to engage in production; or directly sell labor to do short-term work to increase income and supplement the insufficiency of their central enterprise, all of which are called rural sideline occupations. For example, in ordinary rural areas, most farmers cultivate rice and wheat, but planting rice and wheat does not require working all year round, so in the slack farming season, they weave straw sandals, do carpentry, do hawking, and so on. Because rice and wheat cultivation is the central enterprise for their livelihood, it is the principal occupation; weaving straw sandals, doing carpentry, and doing hawking are sideline occupations because they are operated by using spare time and labor. The central enterprise for one's livelihood, planting rice and wheat, is a part of agriculture, and the operators of these sideline occupations are farmers, so it is called rural sideline occupations.

As mentioned above, principal occupations and sideline occupations are two relative terms, which are even more prominent in rural areas. For example, in places with good water conservancy, farmers take rice cultivation as their principal occupation, and rope making and fishing as their sideline occupations; in seaside fishing villages, most of the labor is used to operate the fishing industry, and all the remaining labor is used for cultivation; even in the same village, it is a sideline occupation for household A, but a principal occupation for household B, so the principal occupation and sideline occupation cannot be definitively judged on the basis of the enterprise itself.

Moreover, rural sideline occupations are easily transformed by environmental changes and the encroachment of external forces: for example, in a certain place, most farmers originally took earthwork, woodwork, and sewing as their sideline occupations, but in recent years, due to rural economic bankruptcy and local unrest, etc., those with money have moved into the city, and the remaining poor people cannot afford to build houses or make clothes. Therefore, these earthworkers, carpenters, and tailors have no work to do, and have to change to other sideline occupations to supplement the insufficiency of their principal occupations. For example, the farmers in a certain place used to weave straw sandals as a sideline occupation, but now there is a new job of weaving straw hats, which is more profitable than straw sandals. Therefore, the farmers who used to weave straw sandals as a sideline occupation are now changing to weaving straw hats as a sideline occupation. Furthermore, if the market demand for a certain sideline occupation's products increases significantly, this sideline occupation will become particularly developed; conversely, it will gradually decline, or even disappear. Therefore, rural sideline occupations are constantly changing, constantly rising and falling.

2. Why Promote Rural Sideline Occupations?

(1) Insufficient Cultivated Land In the past, we always said that our country is "vast in territory and rich in resources", but after investigation and statistics, we know that the land is indeed very large, but not all of this vast land is suitable for cultivation. According to Mr. Weng Wenhao: "Due to geographical restrictions, most places in China are not suitable for human life, or cannot accommodate a large population. The Chinese people have to concentrate in a small number of places: (1) the North China Plain (the plains of the Bai River, Yellow River, and Huai River), (2) the middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River Plain, (3) the hills near the above plains, (4) the southeastern coastal areas of Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong, (5) the Sichuan Basin. The total area of the above five regions is 700,000 square miles, accounting for less than 17% of the national area, while the population is 350 million, accounting for more than 83% of the national population, with a total average density of more than 500 people per square mile, far above Japan and Germany, close to the Netherlands, and the population density in the Central Plains and Yangtze regions is even higher than that of the United Kingdom and Belgium, which have the highest population densities in the world. According to the above population density and 4,000 mu per square mile, the area of land that each person can share is 6 mu per person in the Central Plains region, 4.7 mu per person in the Yangtze region, 11 mu per person in the hilly and southeastern coastal regions, and 6.5 mu per person in the Sichuan Basin, with a total average of 6.5 mu per person (as for the regions where each person shares more mu, it is not that the people there are richer, but because the land there is not good). Moreover, in fact, the land that each person gets is not all cultivable, because the above-mentioned mu includes a lot of mountains, lakes, rivers, residences, roads and other areas. If we calculate only from the cultivated land, each person gets only 3 mu of land at most." (Independent Review, Issue 3)

Let's take a look at the estimates of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, which shows that the area of land managed by Chinese farm households is mostly below 10 mu, accounting for 36% of the total number of farm households, followed by 10 mu to 20 mu, accounting for 14%, and 30 mu to 50 mu, accounting for 8%; further, looking at these figures as a whole, farm households below 20 mu account for 61% of the total number of farm households. If each family is calculated with 5 people, then the cultivated land area per person is slightly less than 4 mu, which is roughly the same as Mr. Weng's estimated number. (Detailed estimates are published in the Agricultural Intelligence Report, Year 3, Issue 4)

From the above two estimates, each farmer has an average of only 3 to 4 mu of cultivated land, and all food and clothing must be obtained from it. No matter how land policy experts improve land distribution, the land will not grow more. No matter how agricultural experts improve cultivation methods, it is difficult to produce the output of two mu of land from one mu. Even if one mu can produce the output of two mu of land, each person will only get 6 or 7 mu, which is not enough to maintain a livelihood. According to experts, a farmer needs about 40 mu of cultivated land to maintain a decent life. Therefore, the shortage of cultivated land in our country has reached its extreme. Farmers cannot maintain their livelihoods without seeking remedies from sideline occupations. This is the first reason to promote rural sideline occupations.

(2) Surplus Labor As mentioned above, 150 million farmers are housed in an area of 700,000 square miles. There is little land and a large population, so there is a lot of spare time every year. According to the survey and estimation of Mr. Buck, a professor at Jinling University, the actual time that Chinese farmers spend on crop production each year, if each farmer works 10 hours a day, only needs three months to complete. The remaining nine months are partly wasted. For example, when selling agricultural products, everyone does not try to unite and transport them by boat or truck, but carries them into the city one by one. This not only costs mental and physical labor, but also wastes time, which is really a pity. Part of the time is spent on improper entertainment such as sitting in tea shops and gambling because there is no suitable work to do. Therefore, if so much surplus labor is not used for sideline occupations to increase their income, it will have a great impact on farmers' livelihoods and local order. This is the second reason to promote rural sideline occupations.

(3) Utilization of Residual Materials and Vacant Land As the saying goes, even bricks and wood scraps are useful. Especially in rural areas, there is simply nothing that cannot be used. For example, using green grass from the fields to raise cattle and sheep, which can be sold for money when they grow up, and the manure of cattle and sheep can be used to fertilize the fields, is a very good sideline occupation. We all use mulberry stalks as fuel, but mulberry bark can be used to make paper, which can be peeled off during the slack farming season, or made by oneself, or made together, or even sold to paper mills to increase income. These are all common people who neglect to use residual materials as sideline occupations.

Page 9

Philippine Congress's Bill to Restrict Foreign Business Greatly Affects Overseas Chinese Commerce and Employment The Chinese General Chamber of Commerce Has Lodged an Objection 69

Xiamen Communication: There are more than 140,000 overseas Chinese in the Philippines, most of whom are from southern Fujian. They actually control a very large economic power, and the merchants in the business occupy an absolute advantage. Therefore, the Philippine government is trying its best to restrict the business of overseas Chinese. After the independence of the Philippines, it will tend to be active. Although it is nominally said to restrict foreign merchants, in fact, overseas Chinese account for the largest number of foreign merchants and are also the most powerful. It is tantamount to restricting overseas Chinese only. Li Qingquan, chairman of the Philippine Chinese General Chamber of Commerce and member of the Fujian Provincial Government, arrived in Xiamen on the 13th via Hong Kong, took the Haitan to Xiamen, and stayed at his private residence on Qizhishan, Gulangyu. According to him, "After the independence of the Philippines, the Philippine government is also actively seeking self-sufficiency in the economic field, so it imposes considerable restrictions on foreign businesses. There are many such proposals in the current session of the House of Representatives, many of which are unfavorable to foreign merchants. Although it is not limited to overseas Chinese, the overseas Chinese in the Philippine business market account for a large part of the power. Therefore, what is unfavorable to foreign merchants is unfavorable to overseas Chinese. This time, I am the chairman of the General Chamber of Commerce, and I love to represent the overseas Chinese in the Philippines to raise objections to the Philippine government, (1) Foreign shops that need ten shop assistants can only use two of their own nationals, and the remaining eight must use Filipinos or Americans, and so on proportionally (2) Restricting the number of foreign workers (3) Registering foreign nationals, each person must pay a license fee of 20 Philippine silver dollars (4) Retailers in various places will be operated by non-Filipinos (5) Shop bookkeeping will be changed to Filipino, Spanish, or English This number is related to the lifeblood of overseas Chinese businesses. The purpose of the Philippine government is nothing more than to find a way out for the Filipino people and reduce unemployment. If its various plans are realized, the number of unemployed overseas Chinese will greatly increase, and commerce will also be greatly affected. Now, in addition to the Chamber of Commerce raising objections, I have also explained the reasons to the Philippine authorities in detail and asked them to carefully consider them. The cases have not yet been approved by the Philippine President. It would be fortunate if they could be cancelled." According to the above points, if they are realized, not only will 80-90% of the unemployed overseas Chinese workers reach that level, but the impact on the entire overseas Chinese business will also be extremely great. The Filipinos are inferior to the overseas Chinese in terms of hard work and agility. They cannot compete with the overseas Chinese in terms of industry and commerce. If Filipinos are used instead of employees, shops will also feel a decrease in work efficiency, and the majority of retailers in the entire Philippines are controlled by overseas Chinese. Once business is prohibited, business will largely be at a standstill, and wholesalers will not be able to operate. As for changing bookkeeping to Filipino, Spanish, and English, it is inevitable that foreign accountants must be hired, which is difficult in terms of economy, work, and habits. All of this is related to the entire fate of overseas Chinese businesses and is absolutely unbearable. (September 16)

Decline of the Porcelain Industry in Jingdezhen, Jiangxi The Ministry of Industry Plans to Improve It 70

Nanchang Communication: The porcelain of Jingdezhen, Jiangxi has always been one of the national industries of our country. Even from the Qing Dynasty to the Republic of China, at its peak, there were as many as 150,000 workers directly engaged in the porcelain industry out of a population of 280,000, and the annual output was as high as 15-16 million yuan. Now, due to backward technology, encroachment by foreign porcelain, and years of bandit disasters, production and sales have plummeted. According to people in Jingdezhen who are familiar with the porcelain industry, there are only more than 10,000 people engaged in the porcelain industry now, with an annual output of 4-5 million yuan. More than half of the kiln households have closed down, and those who barely support themselves are also intermittent and struggling to survive. The biggest reasons for its failure are as follows: (1) In terms of raw materials, various porcelain clays are far away in Xingzi, Wuyuan, Qimen, Guixi, Leping, Yugan, and Linchuan, making transportation inconvenient. The materials are also not fine enough, and the composition is difficult to be accurate. The production of pine firewood and charcoal for fuel is limited, and the cost is too expensive. (2) In terms of manufacturing, sticking to old rules and not knowing how to use machinery, and the sagger for holding porcelain is often collapsed because it is not resistant to high heat, which is also a fatal injury. (3) Goods focus on aristocratic works of art, while neglecting civilian daily necessities, so that domestic daily necessities are almost entirely occupied by foreign porcelain. (4) In terms of business, lack of capital, slow transportation and sales, coupled with the competition of gangs, the control of workers, and bad habits are also the reasons for failure. In recent years, the National Economic Commission, the Ministry of Industry, and the industrial and financial circles have had improvement plans, but they are limited by resources and are also talking on paper. This time, Minister of Industry Wu Dingchang visited Jingdezhen and found that the porcelain industry in the area was so dying that not only was the loss to Jiangxi Province too great, but also the national tax was greatly affected. He decided to report to the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Finance to allocate huge sums of money to be handled by the Ministry of Industry in conjunction with the Jiangxi Construction Department to handle improvement matters, and plans to first set up a raw material refining plant for mass production. The capital is divided equally between the province and the country, and the Pottery Bureau has started to carry out this project.

The Guangda Porcelain Company, initiated by the Provincial Government and various industrial circles, has a capital of 1.8 million yuan, and various parties have enthusiastically subscribed for shares. The factory is located in Jiujiang. However, the manager, Du Chongyuan, was imprisoned for hindering foreign relations, and the project was suspended in the middle. The construction of the Xun factory site is about to be completed, and Du has also been released from prison in Shanghai and has come to Xun. He plans to build high-temperature kilns and install instruments and machinery. It is expected that preparations will be completed by the beginning of next spring. The factory will be a completely mechanized industry, refining civilian daily necessities to resist imports, so that the Jingdezhen porcelain industry can gradually develop.

Fujian Province The Initial Stage of Land Consolidation is Completed The First Phase of Five Counties Has Been Completed The Number of Fields in Longxi and Nan'an Has Increased Several Times 71

Xiamen Communication: The collection of field taxes in Fujian Province is still based on the customs of the former Qing Dynasty. The grain series and Ding quota still follow the old customs of many years ago. Therefore, there are often malpractices of grain without land or land without grain. The total cultivated land in the province is estimated to be 20 million mu, but the annual field tax revenue is only 2 million. In fact, the Ding grain surcharge paid by the people is more than one yuan per mu, or even two yuan, which has become an image of official and civilian interaction. In recent years, the financial situation of Fujian Province has been extremely difficult, and there is a lack of ways to increase revenue. The provincial government has therefore carried out land consolidation. It is estimated that if the consolidation is successful, the annual field tax revenue can reach 20 million yuan based on an average of one yuan per mu for 20 million mu in the province. At present, the total revenue of local taxes in Fujian Province is only more than 7 million yuan per year. Land consolidation began last year, and it was hosted by the Department of Civil Affairs, ordering the county governments to handle land reports. However, the results reported are mostly inconsistent with the actual number of mu in each county. Now, the provincial government has specially ordered the Land Administration Bureau to handle the consolidation of the ten land areas, and designated the first phase to consolidate the five counties of Longxi, Nan'an, Yongchun, Huian, and Xianyou first. It started in April this year and was limited to five months. The end of August has been reached. The provincial government sent several land inspection officers to the south to inspect. Gan Zanxu inspected the two counties of Longxi and Nan'an. After Wang completed the inspection, he arrived in Xiamen from Zhangzhou on the 13th. According to him, the inspection results showed that the two counties of Xixi and Jing had increased by more than 10,000 after consolidation compared with the people's hall's investigation and report last year. The former Longxi had only 60,000 to 70,000 mu, but now it has increased three times, reaching more than 200,000 mu, and Nan'an has increased four times, reaching more than 140,000 mu. The reported number of mu and the actual number of mu in Longxi accounted for 80%, and Nan'an accounted for 85% to 90%. The results are really impressive. Now, Nan'an's register can be completed by the end of the month, and Longxi will also stop reporting. The entire project can be completed by the end of October. As for the field tax and Ding grain, Longxi levied 1.2 yuan per mu before consolidation and Nan'an levied 80 cents. After consolidation, Longxi can be reduced to less than one yuan, and Nan'an can be reduced to less than 70 cents. In the future, the Land Reporting Office of each county government and local gentry organizations will be responsible for handling the tax evaluation committee. (September 16)

The Huai River Guidance Association is Building the Honghukou Movable Dam 72

After completion, giant ships can reach Bengbu Bengbu Communication: The Huai River Guidance Association's plan to guide and control the Huai River in recent years is to separate the Yangtze and Huai Rivers into the sea, which is based on the theories of predecessors and the results of on-the-spot surveys as the standard. Its purpose is nothing more than to prevent floods, facilitate shipping, and irrigate farmland. As for the principle of guiding the Huai River, the first priority is to dredge the waterway into the Yangtze River, and use Gongze Lake as a flood control reservoir to regulate floods. The waterway into the Yangtze River is 153 kilometers long. The route goes from Hongze Lake through Sanhe to Jingou Town, turns into Baijiajian, heads to Gaoyou Lake and Tangjia Lake, and then opens a new river, reaches Shaobo Lake from Nanhu, and reaches Liuzha, passes through the canal, and goes out of the Guijiang diversion rivers, taking the Mangdao River and Liaojiagou to Sanjiangying to enter the Yangtze River. It is expected that before excavating the waterway into the Yangtze River, the Sanhe Movable Dam at the mouth of Hongze Lake must be built, and the Honghu Dike and ship lock and spillway gate must be built to control the water volume and make it a navigation channel. Hongze Lake is the water storage area in the lower reaches of the Huai River, and it has the effect of controlling the flow of the Huai River. When preparing to build the movable dam, an engineering bureau was set up in Jiangba to take special responsibility. It is learned that this construction project is contracted by Shanghai Fuxiji Construction Factory. The entire dam is 750 meters long, with 60 holes, each hole is 18 feet wide and 5.5 meters high. The foundation is made of concrete, and the doors are made of steel. Each one can be opened and closed freely, requiring a cost of 3.5 million yuan. Since the start of construction last spring, earthwork engineering has been started first. The earthwork is a total of 5 million cubic meters, of which 800,000 cubic meters have been completed and are still in progress. A total of 17,000 people are working every day, divided into day and night shifts. By the end of June next year, the earthwork engineering can be completed. Piling engineering has now started and will be completed by October next year, and then concrete work will be implemented. The movable dam project can be completed by the end of 1937. In the future, the water level of Honghu can be adjusted at any time. When there is flooding, it will discharge floodwater into the sea. The initial discharge rate is 1,000 to 1,500 cubic meters per second, and it will gradually expand in the future. When there is drought, it will control the flood flow to facilitate irrigation. Both Huai shipping and navigation will benefit from it. Giant ships with a draft of 2 meters and a capacity of 900 tons can sail from the Yangtze River to Sanjiangying, enter Zhangfu River through the Shaobo Huaiyin two ship locks, cross Gong Lake, and pass through the Huai River, and can directly reach Bengbu Huaiyuan and other ports.

Songjiang 73

Small Kunshan Militia Dispute

In Songjiang's Small Kunshan, a dispute arose among the stout men of Dapu Port Village over uniform issues, leading to the destruction of the Small Kunshan Public Security Patrol Station by a crowd and minor injuries to the police chief. Afterwards, Public Security Bureau Chief He Runzhang went to reprimand them, and the stout men resumed their work as usual. Subsequently, County Magistrate Li, considering Yu Fengliang, the chief of the ninth bao of the town, Chen Shixiong, the chief of the second jia of the sixth bao, and farmers Chen Shichang, Shi Lanbo, Xu Musheng, Shi Qin-yu, Yu Deyun, Yu Defu, Xu Rentang, Xu Youtang, Xu Xiangzhou, and village women Xu Xia-shi and Yu Peng-shi, a total of thirteen individuals, as the core members of this riot, specifically ordered Fei Gongxia, the captain of the water patrol team, to arrest and deliver them separately within three days of receiving the order. Captain Fei then led patrol officers, twenty policemen, and security team soldiers, taking boats down to the village to conduct a sweeping arrest. For a time, villagers fled in all directions, and they gained nothing. Afterwards, Yu Defu, also known as Yu Dehu, was successively captured in Songjiang, and after interrogation by the local court, he was released on bail. Recently, Xu Xiangzhou was also arrested, while the remaining criminals are still being pursued. It is now known that Lu Shunong and others from Songjiang residing in Beijing, concerned that the reported arrest of as many as thirteen ringleaders might have widespread implications and affect agricultural affairs, have specially sent a letter to County Magistrate Li appealing to him, wondering if the authorities can understand the hardship of farming and avoid implicating others.

Nanhui 74

Sheep Thief Strangles Housewife

In Huanglou Village, Third District, an elderly woman, Yao Sun-shi, made a living by raising sheep. The night before, a thief broke into her house, intending to steal three sheep. When she discovered him, she loudly shouted for the thief to be caught. Due to living alone, no one came to her aid at the time. The thief, annoyed by her incessant shouting, untied her belt and strangled her to death, then covered her head with a water vat and fled. Yesterday, someone discovered the body and reported it to the district office, which in turn reported it to the county government. The county government dispatched Inspector Li Qingping of the Fourth Sub-station of the Zhuqiao Public Security Bureau, along with a clerk, to conduct an examination, which confirmed the facts. A report has been submitted to apprehend the murderer for further investigation.

Construction of Dike Banks in Various Districts

The dike banks in various districts of this county have gradually collapsed since they were repaired in the twenty-first year. If major floods occur, the damage would be unbearable. Aware of this, the county government has strictly ordered each township head to supervise the farmers and promptly repair the collapsed sections. For larger projects, during the slack farming season in winter, laborers will be organized and built according to the people's labor service regulations in order to prevent floods.

Changshu 77

Hupu Captures Fugitive Criminal

Jin Changkun, a man from out of town, has lived in Hupu Town in this county for a long time. Recently, his nephew reported him for trafficking in a large number of smuggled rayon. The Hupu water police team arrested Jin and sent him to the county. An investigation revealed that Jin had colluded with Shen Sandi and others to rob the Jiu Da Cloth Factory in Hongkou, Shanghai. The latter had already been arrested, but Jin was still hiding here in Hupu. According to his nephew's original report, "Jin Changkun has been hiding in Laichang since the Shanghai case. He lives in Hupu along the river and specializes in trafficking in smuggled goods near Haimen and Chongming. On one occasion, he transported 180 dan of smuggled rayon, packed in sacks, and peddled it around Xu Liujing, making thousands of dollars in profit." Therefore, after Jin was captured, he was sent to the county government. After judicial interrogation, Jin claimed to be from Shandong and had been living in Hupu for a long time, working as a fisherman and loading goods for customers, and he did not engage in the trafficking of smuggled goods. When questioned about the robbery of the Jiu Da Factory in Hongkou, Shanghai, he denied it even more, saying that this was actually his nephew making false accusations because he had failed to get a loan. As a result, he was ordered to be detained pending investigation.

Wuxi 78

Yubao Journalists Come to Wuxi to Petition

The Changshu Telegraph Daily was destroyed by Zhou Tongzhi, the leader of the First Squad of the First Company of the Tenth Security Brigade stationed in Changshu. This was due to a news report on the 7th and 8th of this month about a "brawl at the Dongfang Tea House", which involved security team soldiers. Zhou led forty soldiers to the newspaper office. After the incident, Wang Zipei was dispatched twice by the special commissioner to Changshu to investigate, ordering that Zhou Tongzhi be placed under supervision. Zheng Faxin, the deputy brigade commander, escorted Zhou to Wuxi. After the special commissioner reviewed the case, he ordered him to be detained pending investigation. However, the telegraph office, due to the destruction of the office buildings, was unable to work and live there. Yesterday, a special representative was sent to Wuxi to visit Special Commissioner Zang, requesting a swift resolution to the case and strict punishment of the perpetrators. Section Chief Sheng met with the petition representatives and replied that Special Commissioner Zang was paying close attention to the case and would handle it fairly according to the law in order to protect public opinion. Zhou and others were satisfied and left.

Pump Explosion Tragedy

Yang A-da from Dangkou, Eighth District, used to operate a sweet dew-carrying boat to Wuxi, and also had a water pumping boat. His brothers, Yang Jinsheng and Qiaosheng, were both engaged in farming. Jinsheng's son, A-jin, 22 years old, and Qiaosheng's son, Shigen, 18 years old, helped out with pumping water when they were not busy with farming. A week ago, A-jin and Shigen sailed the boat to the city alone, to the Yongxing Machine Factory in Qiantai Ping Lane outside Guangfu Gate to fit machine parts. Yesterday (the 17th), they were ready to return home. At about 10 a.m., A-jin lit the pump lamp and fired up the engine. The lamp exploded suddenly because the air pressure was too high, and the fire spread to the kerosene tank, causing the entire boat to be engulfed in flames. At that moment, A-jin was in the cabin and Shigen was lying in the boat shed, taking the full impact. Unable to escape, they were burned all over, their skin charred and their flesh roasted. They jumped into the river. Employees from the factory drew water to extinguish the fire. As a result, the machine boat and an ox were burned. The injured men were rescued, carried to the Brothers Hospital for treatment, but due to the severity of the burns, they were barely alive and their lives were in danger. In the afternoon, the factory sent a special representative to the village to report to their families to come to the city to take care of everything.

This seriously endangered the area. On the afternoon of the 16th, Commissioner Zhou went to the wharf north of the city to conduct an inspection and survey, and then crossed the river to inspect the Shixu Port. He returned to the county at about 4 p.m. for a discussion to study the matter in detail, finding that the Zhongxing Wharf did not obstruct the collapse of the dikes north of the river. He will report this fact to the Construction Hall for review.
