The Current State of Overseas Chinese Education in Manila - Despite Financial Difficulties, Schools are Notably Developed, But Each Operates Independently - In Response to Environmental Needs, English and Chinese are Taught Concurrently Starting from the Third Grade of Primary School 165

(Special dispatch from Manila by correspondent Yan Wenchou)

Manila is the capital of the Philippines, home to over 10,000 overseas Chinese (with over 100,000 throughout the Philippine archipelago). Many come with their families, including over 5,000 school-aged children. If all these children were to attend Philippine schools, our overseas Chinese would fulfill their tax obligations and naturally have the right to enjoy education. However, when these children grow up, they would inevitably lose their national identity. If schools were established independently, following the facilities of primary schools in the mainland, there would be issues related to the environment and living skills. Furthermore, it would be impossible to strictly adhere to all regulations issued by the ministry. Therefore, overseas Chinese education has become a major topic. Recently, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission of Nanjing sent its member Li Pusheng and the Ministry of Education sent inspector Fang Zhengyun to inspect education in various regions of Southeast Asia. They first arrived in Manila. The following is a description of the general situation of overseas Chinese education in Manila, which is also what those concerned about overseas Chinese affairs hope for.

(1) The Nascent Stage of Schools

When the United States first governed the Philippines, the first consul, Chen Ziyan (whose father, Chen Qianshan, was a Kapitan during the Spanish colonial era and a Jinshi graduate of the Guangxu era of the Qing Dynasty, assigned as the first consul to the Philippines), established the first school using the original Kapitan's yamen (government office). This is now the Zhongxi School, the oldest (with the most students in day and night classes, totaling 1,200) school in Southeast Asia. Soon after, the Kapitan's yamen was taken over by the American government and attached to the Chinese Charitable Association. At that time, China had not yet promulgated primary school regulations and viewed it as a charitable undertaking. Funding was provided by the Charitable Association. Although English was also taught, the number of students was only thirty or forty. Nevertheless, it represented a rudimentary form of a school in its initial stage. It was not until the spring of the Xinhai Revolution that it became independent from the Charitable Association. After the founding of the Republic of China, it was observed that education in the Philippines was advancing rapidly under American rule, and the people's intelligence was increasing daily. Simultaneously, more overseas Chinese were arriving with their families, and the number of school-aged children was increasing annually. As a result, in 1914, the Overseas Chinese Education Association was established here, levying a business surcharge (methods detailed below) as regular funding. Overseas Chinese schools in Manila gradually increased, and schools were also established in various cities and prefectures, each securing funding locally. Furthermore, most built their own school buildings. Unfortunately, overseas Chinese in various locations, perhaps due to deeply held partisan opinions, could not create a holistic plan for the development of public education. Otherwise, they would not merely be maintaining the status quo.

(2) The Past and Present of the Overseas Chinese Education Association

The association was established in 1914, initially with the prefix "Philippine," but its scope only extended to Manila. Its purpose was to expand overseas Chinese education (at that time, Manila only had the Zhongxi School). Therefore, it proposed levying a business surcharge to fund regular educational expenses. Chinese merchants gladly agreed. Under the local government's tax regulations, merchants had to pay a business tax of one dollar and fifty cents to the government for every one hundred dollars in sales. Simultaneously, an additional four and a half cents were levied as a regular fee for overseas Chinese education. This was collected quarterly every three months by the Likin Bureau (tax collection agency). This was something that any store could afford. During its peak, it generated over 100,000 dollars annually. The schools managed by the Education Association included one middle school, one girls' school, and six ordinary primary schools, with over 2,000 students in day and night classes. However, the business surcharge was voluntary and lacked a legal basis. Recently, the finances of overseas Chinese schools in Manila have become increasingly strained, forcing them to consider merging schools (leaving only one middle school, one girls' school, and primary schools). The business surcharge has been decreasing year by year. The reasons for this decrease are nothing more than (1) acting impulsively, (2) poor business conditions, and (3) emulation of others, resulting in annual revenue of no more than five or six thousand dollars this year. The Education Association bears the expenses of these schools and can only raise temporary funds to maintain the status quo.

(3) The Relationship between the Education Association and the Schools Under Its Jurisdiction

Overseas Chinese schools in British and Dutch territories often experience internal conflicts, with school boards controlling the power to hire personnel. Teachers often have their own backers, and principals lack the authority to manage the entire school. As a result, turmoil often erupts. In the case of the Manila Education Association, it only hires the principal. All other staff members and teachers within the school are recommended by the principal, and the board does not interfere with internal administration. Therefore, the educational sector is stable, with over half of the staff having served for more than a year. Some principals have served for over twenty years. This is not because the board of directors is abandoning its responsibilities but because it trusts the principal. However, this has led to a backlash from public opinion, which accuses the Education Association of being controlled by powerful figures and having lost its authority, merely being responsible for raising funds for the four schools under its jurisdiction. As a reporter on the side of the school, I dare not make a strong judgment on right and wrong.

(4) The Special Development of Overseas Chinese Schools in Manila

Despite the Education Association's financial difficulties, overseas Chinese primary schools have sprung up like bamboo shoots after the rain, showing remarkable development. Currently, in terms of school units, there are a total of 23 schools, some with dozens of students, others with one or two hundred, and the largest with nearly three hundred (excluding the four schools under the Education Association). The reason is that many of the former staff members of these schools have emotional ties and cannot be easily replaced, leaving no vacancies for newcomers. Moreover, many graduates of Minnan University's high school take Southeast Asia as their destination. However, their skills are not suited to the business environment, so they flock to the field of education. With too many monks and not enough gruel, they inevitably have to start their own ventures to support themselves. It is speculated that this is not far from the truth.

(5) The Distribution of English and Chinese Courses in Overseas Chinese Schools

According to the primary school curriculum standards required by the Ministry of Education, there is no foreign language subject. However, overseas Chinese schools are permitted to teach foreign languages starting from the fifth grade of primary school to adapt to the local living environment. Zhongxi, Zhongzhong, Puzhi, and No. 2 Primary Schools in Manila have the most students and the longest history among overseas Chinese schools. In the past, they devoted the mornings to Chinese language instruction and the afternoons to English language instruction, which has drawn much criticism from educators in the motherland. However, to explain the reasons for teaching Chinese and English separately in the morning and afternoon, it is necessary to start with the environmental factors. Since being enlightened by the United States, Filipinos have mastered English. Most overseas Chinese merchants deal directly with foreigners, and sales documents, transportation bills, and various labels are all in English. Recently, bookkeeping laws have been implemented, so clerks in the business world need to have a basic understanding of both English and Chinese. Overseas Chinese schools have been teaching both English and Chinese concurrently since the third grade of primary school, aiming for students to reach the seventh-grade English level by the time they graduate from junior high school. With a little training, they can handle all bookkeeping, typing, and import/export documents used in stores. This is unlike graduates from mainland junior high schools, who have to start from scratch when they enter the business world here. Therefore, many who are unaccustomed to business life flock to the field of education. Twenty years ago, English was an optional subject in overseas Chinese schools. Following the regulations of the ministry, a few hours were added each week starting from the fifth grade. However, most merchants felt that the skills were not useful and sent their children to Philippine schools. Weighing the pros and cons, even if overseas Chinese schools do not focus entirely on Chinese language, is it not better than sending them to Philippine schools to study foreign languages entirely?

The above is a discussion of the state of overseas Chinese education in Manila, the capital of the Philippines. As for the results of its management, the two inspectors, Li and Fang, will undoubtedly provide a detailed report after returning to China.

Higher Education in Jiangxi Province in 1934 166

The status of provincial vocational schools and students studying abroad in higher education in Jiangxi Province in 1934 is detailed below. (1) Vocational schools include the Medical Vocational School, the Industrial Vocational School (also offering higher vocational courses equivalent to secondary school), and the Agricultural Vocational School (also offering higher and junior agricultural and forestry courses equivalent to secondary school). The Medical Vocational School has three grades, with 52 male students and 7 female students, 38 faculty and staff members, and an annual expenditure of 41,803 yuan. The Industrial Vocational School has four grades (plus eight grades in higher vocational courses), with 39 male and female students (plus 218 in higher vocational courses), 63 faculty and staff members, and an annual expenditure of 80,157 yuan. The Agricultural Vocational School has one grade (plus higher and junior agricultural and forestry courses in two grades), with 6 students (plus 69 in agricultural and forestry courses), 22 faculty and staff members, and an annual expenditure of 1,100 yuan. In total, these three schools have eight grades (plus 11 grades in the attached secondary school programs), with 104 students (plus 87 in secondary school programs), 123 faculty and staff members, and an annual expenditure of 126,160 yuan.

(2) Students studying engineering abroad include 18 in Japan, 1 in Germany, 1 each in France and Belgium, and 5 in the United States, totaling 28. Students studying liberal arts include 13 in Japan, 3 in France, and 1 each in the United States and England, totaling 18. Students studying science include 15 in Japan, 3 in Germany, and 1 in France, totaling 19. Students studying law and politics include 2 in Japan, 2 in France, and 1 each in Germany, the United States, and England, totaling 10. Students studying commerce include 2 each in Japan, Germany, and the United States, totaling 6. Students studying medicine include 11 in Japan, 3 in Germany, and 1 in France, totaling 15. Students studying education include 6 in Japan, 2 in England, and 1 each in France and the United States, totaling 10. There are also 2 students studying agriculture in Belgium, 2 studying art in Japan, 1 studying physical education in Germany, and 6 studying other subjects, including 3 in Japan and 1 each in France, the United States, and England. In total, there are 72 students in Japan, 13 in Germany, 12 in France, 11 in the United States, 3 in Belgium, and 1 in Switzerland. In 1934, there were a total of 117 students studying abroad, with 63 supported by public funds, 8 partially supported by public funds, 5 receiving subsidies, 2 receiving Boxer Indemnity grants, and 39 self-funded. According to statistics from the Ministry of Education, there were only 621 students studying abroad from all provinces and cities in China in 1933. Jiangxi Province alone had 117 students studying abroad in 1934, so Jiangxi has a relatively large number of students studying abroad compared to other provinces and cities in the country.

General Report of the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary and Normal School Subject Research Association 168

Order issued by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an order to the education bureaus of various counties yesterday stating, "After reviewing the organization and development of the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary and Normal School Subject Teaching Research Committee, as well as the resolutions passed by the various groups in their meetings, all have been separately notified by this department and sent to the relevant schools for comments, all of which are on file. Now that the research and organization work of each group has been completed, the general reports of all groups have been submitted one after another. After careful reading, the contents include meticulous discussions and specific solutions to various issues related to teaching in each subject, which is truly a great achievement in education in this province. A summary of the general reports of each group is now printed and distributed. Apart from the various issues that will be kept by this department for reference, those concerning the allocation of teaching time, such as cases 1, 7, and 8 of the mathematics group, and item 4 of the physics and chemistry group regarding the appropriate level of detail and time allocation for each part of the teaching materials, which involve changes to the standards issued by the ministry and the teaching progress, should be implemented by each school as appropriate, and the implementation opinions should be reported before the end of the semester for verification. Furthermore, regarding various issues concerning teaching equipment, such as the equipment standards set by the history and geography group, each school should handle them properly, taking into account the actual situation. As for the remaining practical issues concerning teaching materials, teaching methods, assignments, grading, remediation for low-achieving students, and other practical issues, all of which are essential, the principals of each school should supervise the teachers of each subject in 1936 to earnestly comply with and implement them, in order to improve scientific methods and increase educational effectiveness. In the future, when inspectors from this department conduct inspections, this will be used as the basis for evaluating teaching in each subject. In addition to separate orders, a copy of each organization's general report is now sent. It is ordered that the director of each bureau should immediately comply with this order and instruct the secondary and normal schools under their jurisdiction to comply as well. This order is issued."

The Columbia University Alumni Association has been established for nearly a year, and there are currently nearly one hundred members. Science Society of China Establishes Science Awards 170

Hu Xiansu, Li Zhaohuan, and others serve as committee members

To encourage interest in scientific research among Chinese people

At the annual meeting held by the Science Society of China in Beiping on August 16 this year, the board of directors proposed that in addition to the existing various donated awards, a Science Society of China Award be established, consisting of a gold medal and a certificate, to be awarded to the Chinese person with the most significant achievements in scientific research each year at the annual meeting. The proposal was approved by the general meeting, and Hu Xiansu (biological sciences) was appointed as the chairman, with Hu Gangfu (physical sciences), Gu Yuxiu (engineering sciences), and Li Zhaohuan (social sciences) as committee members. A Science Society of China Award Committee was established to be responsible for handling all matters.

Vocational Education Society and Vocational Guidance Institute Seek Teachers 171

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute of the China Vocational Education Society has recently been entrusted by a secondary school in another city to recruit a high school business teacher. The candidate must be a graduate of a well-known church university with a degree in business, a Christian, possess a cooperative spirit, and have teaching experience to be qualified. The teaching load is 22 hours per week, with a salary starting at 60 yuan per month, without room and board. In addition, someone has entrusted the institute to recruit a physical education and martial arts teacher. The candidate must be a graduate of a physical education school, proficient in various martial arts, have good character, and be amiable to be qualified. The salary is negotiable. Furthermore, a vocational school in this city has entrusted the institute to recruit a full-time high school mechanical engineering teacher. The candidate must be a graduate of a domestic or foreign university with a degree in mechanical engineering, hold a formal diploma, and have extensive experience to be qualified. Also, a part-time civil engineering teacher is needed. The candidate must be a graduate of a domestic or foreign university with a degree in civil engineering, have extensive construction experience, and be skilled in teaching to be qualified. The teaching load is 10 hours per week, and the salary is negotiable. In addition, a provincial normal school in Anhui Province has entrusted the institute to recruit a female sewing and handicraft teacher. The candidate must be a graduate of a sewing and embroidery program, have extensive experience, have new ideas, be able to tailor various garments and children's clothing, and be skilled in teaching crafts to be qualified. The salary is 70 to 80 yuan per month, with room and board provided. Furthermore, a county high school in Fujian Province has entrusted the institute to recruit a physical education and military training teacher. The candidate must be a graduate of a physical education school, have extensive teaching experience, and have documentary proof to be qualified. The salary is 30 yuan per month, with room provided but no board, and the travel expenses are self-provided, requiring 12 yuan. In addition, someone has entrusted the institute to recruit a university physics professor. The candidate must be a graduate of a European or American university, hold a master's or doctoral degree in science, and have teaching experience to be qualified. The salary is 200 yuan per month. Also, a district office near Shanghai has entrusted the institute to recruit a physician. The candidate must hold a medical license and be skilled in internal medicine to be qualified. The salary is 40 yuan per month. Those who believe they meet the requirements of any of the above positions and are capable of performing the duties must personally submit a written statement of their education and experience to the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute at 80 Hualong Road within two days of the announcement. Late submissions will not be considered.

Xie Lin Succeeds Yang Yinpu as Dean of the Guanghua Business School 172

Yang Yinpu, the Dean of the Business School of Guanghua University, has been teaching since the school's founding. He has been the Dean of the Business School for the past year. He has now been hired by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to serve as an economic specialist for the League of Nations delegation and is scheduled to depart for Europe in October. The university tried unsuccessfully to persuade him to stay and invited Xie Lin to succeed him. Xie Lin has held important positions such as Chief Accountant of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications and Secretary-General of the Central Bank. He is currently the chairman of the banking department at the university. It is also reported that Yang will continue to handle school affairs as usual before departing for Europe.

Guohua Secondary School on Gordon Road and Zhengfeng Secondary School on Yaozhu Road in Shanghai held a joint dining meeting for the faculty and staff of the two schools at the Huibin Restaurant to discuss technical cooperation between the two schools. Prominent local figures and educational administrators were invited to provide guidance. Those in attendance included Ma Chonggan, Jiang Jianbai, Hu Shuyi, Ling Xianwen, Shen Jiesheng, Wang Yuzhang (Principal of Guohua), Hu Changzhi (Principal of Zhengfeng), as well as faculty, staff, and student parent representatives from both schools, totaling over 100 people. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves in an atmosphere of clinking glasses and toasting.

White Goose Painting School Seeks Students 175

The White Goose Painting School is the only art school in Shanghai that offers part-time instruction. Since the beginning of the fall semester, the organizers, including Chen Qiucao, Fang Xuegu, and Pan Sitong, have strived to improve various facilities. In addition to hiring new writers Cheng Jie and He Tingcan as instructors, they have also personally taken on teaching duties, so that beginners can receive good training in basic practical skills and advance systematically for real benefits. Many new and old students are studying with excitement, and the number of participants is increasing daily. Recently, a new room has been opened, using reflected light to depict models of teaching objects at night, with particularly thoughtful designs. It is reported that there are still vacancies available. Anyone with a passion for art, whether or not they have studied painting, is welcome to join. The school is located at No. 3, Lane 364, Avenue Edward VII, near Chengdu Road. Please send two cents in postage for the prospectus.

Tea is Being Planned for Promotion 176

The Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea General Sales Office, with only about seven or eight thousand boxes of unsold tea in stock, is aiming to clear out its remaining inventory to quickly conclude its operations and is striving for a comprehensive sales push. In recent days, Mr. Cheng Zhenji, the manager of the office, has repeatedly convened meetings to discuss countermeasures and negotiate prices with foreign firms such as British-owned Jardine Matheson, Ewo, and Gibb Livingston, as well as the Yutai Tea Shop, for small-scale transactions, which are currently at a standstill. As for the green tea market, there have also been no major transactions, with only needle-shaped, eyebrow-shaped, and high-grade "Chouxin Zhenmei" teas experiencing slight sales, with prices remaining stable.

According to a report from the Tea Trade Association, the green tea market appears rather dull, and a quick turnaround is unlikely. Yesterday, foreign firms, due to receiving telegrams from overseas with tighter price quotes for "Chouzhen" and "Zhenmei" teas, did not conclude any deals at the discussed prices. However, the "Gongxi Baitu" business was relatively active, with prices similar to before, as well as sales of 11-yuan "Zhucha" teas on Tongfu Road.

Shen Bao Literary Supplement

Gold Standard Market Oscillates Before Falling Slightly 177

Yesterday's gold market initially stabilized before weakening. Major players' supply and demand differed, leading to a rather confusing market situation with much oscillation in the middle. Surface activity loosened, and the market eventually retreated by a small fraction. In the morning, overseas silver markets showed London rising and the US remaining flat. Mond Nickel forward silver prices remained unchanged across the board. Exchange rates initially narrowed before rising. London bullion rose two and a half pence. Bank postings revealed both British and American currencies unchanged. Customs gold unit rose by two li. The standard gold price was posted at 1118.5 yuan. At the market's opening, many sellers immediately started selling, pushing the market downwards. Despite much oscillation in the middle, confidence remained weak, and bearish sentiment prevailed. Spot houses slightly supplied silver bars. HSBC's postings revealed both British and American currencies unchanged, continuing the downward trend. Silver equalization tax was announced to increase by half a point before stabilizing slightly. Then, major buyers started to become active, gradually stabilizing the market. At noon, the trend recovered upward, with the afternoon market striving for supply-demand balance and much struggle. The market was extremely mediocre. More sellers emerged in the afternoon. Indian silver was initially quoted down three annas, but the second quote remained unchanged. As a result, the trend slightly weakened. The October/November futures were posted by the bullish side at 2.89 yuan. Today's market situation is recorded below. Opening price was 1124.8 yuan, up eight jiao from the previous close. Ding Kangfu and Yong sold, retreating to four yuan. Xianghe Yuanmao Yongyi and others bought bars, rising to 4.4 yuan. Tongtaichang and Chunyuan Yong sold bars, falling to 3.7 yuan. Tongfu and others once reached 4.2 yuan. Jingfu San Duo Shengyuan Yong and others sold off. Although HSBC postings showed British and American currencies unchanged, it retreated to 3.3 yuan. Silver equalization tax was announced to increase by half a point before stabilizing slightly. Yuanchang Yongda Decheng Yiyu Daheng Jiuda and others rushed to buy. The noon closing price rose to 1124.1 yuan.

The afternoon market opened at 1123.9 yuan. Yuanmao Yong sold down to 3.8 yuan. Tongfu accepted bars, rising to four yuan. Yuanmao Yong Xianghe Zhengchang jointly sold off. Although Yingfeng Heng accepted bars, the closing price still fell to 1123.6 yuan.

The closing price for Central Bank gold standard was raised to 1118.5 yuan. In terms of closing prices, it rose by approximately five yuan plus. This month's registered price is 1118 yuan, October's is 1121 yuan, and November's is 1124 yuan. Morning makeup water is 1118 yuan, fine gold is increased by six yuan to 1130.8 yuan. Spot market conditions are stable. The buying price for fine gold is increased by nine yuan, and the selling price is thirteen yuan. It is heard that Shengyuan Yong once bought 350 taels. Tianjin goods are increased by 10.05 yuan, but there were no transactions.

Yesterday, the bullish side negotiated with Feng Yongyu Xinxiang Dachangxiang to give Dah Heng Qianchangxiang 2.8 yuan for the swaps. Later, Daheng countered by posting, rising to 2.9 yuan. Jingfu Ding Kangfu Shun posted to buy in. Transactions were scarce.

There were not many transactions in the market. In summary, Daheng Yiyu Dacheng Qiaofeng Yong Tongfu Yingfeng Zhihui Xiang Demao Yong Yongde and others were on the buying side. Chunyuan Yong Qianchangxiang Shengyuan Yong Hengyu Qingfa Yong Fuxing Yong Tongfeng Heng Zhengjin Yuanmao Yong Fu'an Ding Kang Jingfu and others were on the selling side. The market situation for the day was stable and confusing. The market opened in the morning at 1124.8 yuan and closed in the afternoon at 1123.6 yuan. The highest price was 1124.8 yuan, and the lowest price was 1123.3 yuan, a fluctuation of 1.5 yuan. As a result, there was a setback of four jiao. This month, there are 595 remaining bars, with eight bullish parties and five bearish parties. In November, there are 1253 remaining bars, with twelve bullish parties and eleven bearish parties. November futures have 7000 castings, with 26 bulls and 41 bears. The total number of transactions was 1001 bars in the morning and 301 bars in the afternoon.

Foreign Exchange Supply and Demand Fair; Swaps Open, Forwards Slightly Tight 178

The exchange market yesterday saw swaps opening up, resulting in flat-near, tight-far rates. According to morning overseas reports, London forwards were up .0625 for near terms, and flat for far terms. New York silver market was unchanged. Mond Nickel's forward silver prices remained unchanged across the board. London bullion rose two and a half pence. British currency versus US currency narrowed by .25. British currency versus French currency fell by one pound sterling. US currency versus British currency rose by .1875. US currency versus French currency narrowed by .0625. Central Bank postings were revealed; British and American currencies were flat. Customs gold units rose by two li. The exchange market opened in the morning with near-term selling prices of British exchange at 1 shilling, 2 and 25/100 pence and 3125/10000 pence respectively, and US exchange at 20.125 yuan, which were the same as the previous close, indicating that British and American currencies were flat. After the opening, banks slightly tightened, while foreign banks bought in East Asian currency. HSBC's postings revealed both British and American currencies were flat, and the market oscillated. Later, banks still had a selling appetite. Silver equalization tax was announced to increase by half a point, and confidence remained stable. Banks did swaps, and the trend wavered. The afternoon market also appeared confusing. In the afternoon market, banks did forward trades on shillings but remained flat. Japanese banks continued to buy, and East Asian currency transactions were relatively rare. Indian silver was initially quoted down three annas, but the second quote remained unchanged, but had a definite influence. By the close, near-term selling prices were 1 shilling, 2 and 28125/100000 pence for British exchange, and 30.125 yuan for US exchange, which were the same as the previous close, indicating that British and American currencies were flat. For forward terms, British was tight by .03125, and US was tight by .0625, which was due to swaps opening up. Chinese merchants and banks had equal supply and demand. Today's transactions are recorded below.

British exchange opened in the morning with a near-term selling price of 1 shilling, 2 and 28125/100000 pence. Citibank covered September at 28125/100000 pence. Shanghai sold to Zhengjin September at 28125/100000 pence. Holland covered October at .25. In the afternoon market, Overseas Chinese sold to McCarly the first half of November at .25. Overseas Chinese sold to Citibank at the same month and price. Shanghai sold to Citibank November at .25. The closing selling price was 1 shilling, 2 and 28125/100000 pence for spot, and 25 and 28125/100000 pence respectively for October pairing, 21875/100000 and 25 respectively for November pairing, 1875/100000 and 21875/100000 respectively for December pairing. Buying prices were increased accordingly.

US exchange opened in the morning with a near-term selling price of 30.125 yuan. Dongya covered September at .125. Shanghai sold to Sumitomo December at 29.9375 yuan. Shanghai Citibank covered at the same month and price. Citibank covered January at .875. Citibank bought spot at 30.21875 yuan and covered January at 30 yuan. McCarly bought spot at .1875 and covered December at 30 yuan. The noon selling price was 30.125 yuan. In the afternoon market, Yau Lee bought October at .125. Citibank covered January at 29.875 yuan. The closing selling price was 30.125 yuan for spot, .09375 for October, .03125 for November, 29.96875 yuan for December. Through prices were increased by .0625.

Securities and Bond Market Turns Bullish; 96 Bonds Break the Ten Yuan Barrier Again 179

Yesterday at the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange, the market turned bullish, and trading was slightly more active. Market sentiment also turned bullish. The surface was in a situation where it was easy to rise but difficult to fall. Any good news would lead to a high rebound more easily than a fall. However, the overall trend was not optimistic. Yesterday, at the opening, No. 10 and No. 43 were bought in, No. 11 was also in demand, and No. 14 and No. 35 were slightly sold off. Market prices unanimously rose by 0.15 to 0.3 yuan. Before the final decision, the front row continued to rise by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan, and the back row was flat. At the afternoon opening, the situation was still very stable, and covering shorts and swaps were very lively. Generally, it continued to be good by 0.15 yuan. At the closing, retail investors still had demand, and the surface was still more demanding than supplied, and then it was good by 0.15 yuan. There were rumors about the 96 public bonds, and No. 13 was quite in demand, and then it rushed out of the 10 yuan mark again. As a result, the market price rose by 0.15 to 0.45 yuan. The total number of transactions was 5.39 million yuan. The result of the rise and fall is compared and listed on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan).

Cotton Yarn and Flower 180

#### Low Inventory; Yarn Market Sees Resurgence of Bullish Sentiment; Industry is Now in a Bullish Position

The yarn market turned firm and saw a resurgence of bullish sentiment. Because the inventory of various factories is low, the chips for delivery this month are insufficient, the market is stable, and buyers are active, so the market has recovered. Moreover, most of the industry is in a bullish position, but some have turned from bullish to bearish.

#### Standard Yarn Rises Around Two Yuan

At the opening of the standard yarn market in the previous market, the prices of various months showed a slight upward trend. Because there was a lack of sellers in the market, the surface was dry, and the momentum became tighter. After the second round, the price rose step by step, but the trading was not active. Mingde and Changfeng bought in, and the sellers were scattered. Yuda, Runkang, and Dachangcheng, etc., had small amounts. By the closing, the rising wind was very strong. The reason for the rise was entirely due to the chip relationship. As a result, the standard yarn rose by 1.1 to 1.3 jiao in each month compared with the closing price of the previous day. The market was quite tight at the opening in the afternoon, and the price of the three-product yarn rose. General retail investors scrambled to cover shorts, and the market price slowly advanced. As a result, the price of each month increased by 0.6 to 0.7 jiao to 1.1 jiao compared with the morning closing price. It is checked that Deda issued 500 packages, Jifeng 800 packages, Yuda 900 packages, Wang Taixing 1,050 packages, Runkang 900 packages, Yuanda 650 packages, Jinchang 700 packages, Gengfeng 1,700 packages, and Senkang 1,600 packages. Mingde bought 1,050 packages, Shenji 1,900 packages, Changfeng 3,650 packages, Juxing 1,800 packages, Hengchang 800 packages, Dachang 650 packages, and Tonghe 600 packages. The highest and lowest prices for the day are listed on the left.

Poetry Offering 197

— Chen Yin

—Five Years of Wounds—

(Prologue)

I sorrow, I have read, I have heard,

I have also seen, these several pieces,

Filled with brutal and sorrowful poems:

In the flow of my simple and peaceful life,

I cannot accommodate these many real and inaccessible,

Cursable, terrifying impacts.

I must strive to push it out!

(I)

"On the streets,

Thugs run rampant:

Mad and evil

Laughter fills the air;

Fierce and cruel

Faces are menacing.

On the waist

Swords clang;

On the guns

Bayonets are white and gleaming.

Countless

Heads fly;

Innumerable

Corpses lie in rows.

Countless groups of

Women are raped;

Countless piles of

Infants are burned alive.

Countless boxes of

Wealth are plundered;

Countless mountains, rivers, fields, villages, towns... are all swallowed whole.

No sound of chickens or dogs is heard,

Birds and sparrows flee in terror...

In Shenyang city,

Ghosts cry and gods wail;

On Shenyang city,

The Rising Sun flag kisses the sun."

(II)

What is this?—Brutality!

What is this?—Brutality!—

Horrible!—

The devastating sound of "September 18th."

(III)

Brutality—I cannot bear to read!

Brutality—I cannot bear to hear!

Brutality—I cannot bear to see!

I want to curse—

This cannot but be a terrifying and sinful program!

I want to exclaim—

This cannot but be a terrifying and sinful miracle!

I want to deny its existence!

I want to deny its existence!

(IV)

Which evil ghost created this?

This is actually the God of History,

Deliberately attaching it to the body of the peaceful?

Ugliness—we must destroy!

Humiliation—how can we endure it?

(V)

I want to borrow the mouth of the Rain God,

To wash away our humiliation!

I want to borrow the hand of the Wind God,

To sweep away all ugliness!

(VI)

(A trembling and strong feeling,

I am stung by the painful topic of this "September 18th":

Five years of wounds!)

(VII) Five years of wounds!…

"But we must survive!"

"People who do not want to be slaves!"

Let us sing a powerful slogan poem:

"We must fight! We must fight!"

Between Mother and Son 198

— Li Huiying

After old Mrs. Wang got up, she felt as if she had lost something from her whole body. What was it, she couldn't say, but the fact was that there was something missing from her. She tried her best to search, tried her best to ponder, planning to discover the reason, but no, the person was still her body, and her internal organs wouldn't lose one after sleeping for one night. She wore as many clothes as usual, so what else was worth hesitating about? Maybe she was confused herself. When people get old, all kinds of ridiculous things will play tricks on that old body, so it is inevitable that such strange feelings will arise out of nothing.

The brilliance of the hot morning sun of midsummer in July had already poured into the window, and the house was magnificent. Through the light waves, countless dust particles flew, just like the whirlwind rolling up in the blue sky. The difference was that these dust particles were always dancing there, with the arrogance of relatives as if rooted down. When the fresh air drifted into the house, the moldy dampness inside was buried, and old Mrs. Wang did not cough dryly because of the poor air. She had already experienced this point, which was the main reason why she particularly preferred the summer morning to the winter morning. She often said to the neighbors in the same yard: "Once summer comes, I will be resurrected. In winter, I am sick and uncomfortable. The air is good in summer."

At this time, the two neighbors in the yard had also gotten up, and the children were digging in the center of the yard, some were defecating, and some were staring greedily at the jujube tree. The women were lighting coal briquette stoves, and coal smoke floated into the sky like fog, and the fresh air was suddenly dyed turbid. Old Mrs. Wang started cleaning the house as usual, then picked up a piece of worn rag and wiped the dust off the window cover. When she picked up the mirror that had accompanied her for more than forty years to wipe the dust off the mirror surface, she suddenly cried out. It was a cry of surprise, and it showed that things happened suddenly. At that time, the mirror she had personally selected, a dowry item with many years of history, slipped gently out of her hand and fell to the ground, followed by a clear and crisp shattering sound, and the mirror shattered. She was stunned for a while, staring straight with her old eyes, raising her thin hands and staring blankly, not knowing what she was thinking. When she suddenly turned to go to her son's room in the west room, she shouted out a jumble of words: "Ah, the bracelet... Oh God, my bracelet... Did that evil thing steal it?... The Heavenly Lord will not agree... I want the bracelet..."

The west room was empty, and there was no sign of her son. Where did her son go? He used to sleep until the sun was high, why did he get up earlier than her today and go straight away? She originally wanted to ask her son if he had seen her bracelet. In this way, she completely understood the truth of the matter; she was angry, she was heartbroken, she jumped and beat her chest for a while, and even slapped the empty quilt where her son slept several times, as if this would relieve her hatred, and then she cried. There was no doubt that her son pulled it off her arm while she was sleeping last night, and he had long since sold it for a long time and squatted in the white flour house to live a debauched life. Old Mrs. Wang attached great importance to this bracelet. Although it was not necessarily worth much money, it was also a dowry item, and she wanted to bring it with her when she was buried in the soil in the future. With such a thought in mind, she regarded the bracelet as her second life. Just because her son was addicted to bad habits, she didn't know how many things he had stolen from her and exchanged for money to smoke white flour; her old partner died early, and seeing her adult son giving her all kinds of disappointments, she had long since canceled her hope for him in the future, not wanting to rely on his support, and prepared to end her life by herself. When a son grows up, he is no longer his own son. Mother says many good words in vain, and persuasion, agitation, and scolding are all useless. After she was discouraged, she occupied another camp and treated her son as an enemy, always guarding against him and not letting him get close. Since she had no power to exercise active control, she had to come up with this method of resistance from a passive perspective. In this way, her son still often seized an unexpected opportunity to steal her things that she thought were strictly guarded. Her son is really not a good son, her son makes his mother too sad, her son is obsessed with evil things...

As soon as the neighbors heard old Mrs. Wang's crying, many residents guessed what had happened again. Mrs. Zhang, Mrs. Li, and several children all ran over to explore the situation. After they found out, they tried to persuade her and asked the old lady to calm down. They also said by example: "Isn't it your son who stole our things too?" But today's old Mrs. Wang refused to be persuaded and continued to cry, still patting her chest and jumping, while shouting: "This is the only piece of jewelry left, you evil creature, you stole your mother's heart, the Heavenly Lord cannot forgive you, may the Heavenly Lord strike him dead with lightning." At this time, as if she had thought of a way, she ran out of the gate with a snotty nose and tears, only to hear her repeatedly saying: "I'm going to find that evil creature, I'm going to settle the score with him, I'm going to settle the score with him, talk some sense, find a place to reason."

When old Mrs. Wang ran to the entrance of the white flour house, Mrs. Zhang and Mrs. Li followed behind. They were purely worried about the old lady's unexpected behavior, fearing that some other unfortunate things would be caused by this rush - old people, death is like a shadow following them, and when there is a suitable opportunity, they will seize the life of the old. Taking this into account, they were willing to put down their own family affairs and come to fulfill their obligations to take care of this old neighbor. Old Mrs. Wang stopped at the entrance. The door was open, the window was open, and her son was sitting in the house smoking white flour, and he didn't move when he saw her, only talking idly with the XX people. She rushed in and shouted, "Xiao Quan, give me back my bracelet, you undying evil ghost, come out quickly!..." Before she could finish shouting, the XX people slapped her thin left cheek. She only felt a burst of dizziness in front of her eyes and ran out of the door. But she immediately recovered her spirits. She wanted to find her son to reason, and she also wanted to question the XX people, so she ran to the sub-bureau like a gust of wind.

"Old... Chief," she said stammeringly and out of breath, "My... son... smokes white flour... I went to the white... flour house... The XX people hit me... All are... not... unreasonable... Chief... You... for... for... for me... vent this anger..." She couldn't go on, she was like a ball of cotton, and suddenly collapsed onto the bench.

When the chief explained that their powers could not be exercised in the white flour house and could not go to the XX people's house to handle the case, old Mrs. Wang was so angry! What kind of talk was this! How could chiefs say such things! If the chiefs don't care about these things, then who should care?…

The time had reached nine o'clock. Just as old Mrs. Wang was about to refute the chief's unreasonable words that day, she was suddenly stopped by the sound of drums outside the door, and at this time, she saw that in the parade advertising team of XX eye medicine, there was her son inside. She was so happy that it was like opening a bright door, and she shouted, "Chief, this time it's good, my son is in that crowd. The one in green clothes, wearing a three-pointed hat on his head, holding a sign, catch him this time."

"This time it won't work either. Although it's on the street, because there are XX people in charge, that team is full of white flour addicts, so we can't do anything. If you go to grab him, it will cause negotiations, and this can't be done at all"! The chief persuaded, "Old lady, he is always your own son. Go home tomorrow and persuade him well."

"Isn't this without law? Alas! My God..." She stretched out her hand and patted her left cheek, watched the colorful advertising team in the past, and cried again.

Leaving Tokyo 199

— Shan

Amidst the bustling footsteps and waving white handkerchiefs, I left Tokyo, where half the sky was dyed blood red at night.

I met my friend Kuroda-kun in the train. He is a student in the Department of Chinese Literature, specializing in modern Chinese literature; when you meet a foreign friend in a lonely train, you can always have a sense of nostalgia, let alone drinking beer in the train dining car late at night, talking about his beloved poems and his double life.

In foreign life, what you can feel most is your own pitifulness and loneliness, just like a swallow that has just left the nest. On the one hand, it is attached to the old beams of the nest, but on the other hand, it is disgusted with this ordinary life and has great ambitions for everything else.

But at the same time, we can also see and feel the pitiful and small life of this strong neighbor—a dual life; I can especially feel it deeply from the mind and body of Kuroda-kun, this intellectual.

Kuroda-kun deeply hates war and often dreams of a peaceful life. Perhaps because he has suffered too much harm from the education of talent, he has not yet fully understood the war. However, in such times and circumstances, being able to hate war is already something that makes me feel satisfied and happy.

However, the so-called national life often obliterates people's individuality and freedom. Kuroda-kun abandoned this summer research life and went to his hometown of Shikoku, which is full of pine trees. This was sacrificed to the conscription order in times of emergency.

When it comes to imitating war, but you must imitate and prepare not from specializing in war, that kind of contradiction that obliterates one's life is often the foundation of tragedy.

Kuroda-kun is performing this scene of the tragedy on this stage. In the eyes of others, this may be an interesting and varied comedy, but in my eyes, who knows the taste of the dual life: Kuroda-kun's heart is probably covered with clouds of summer-like sorrow!

"The deadline is short, but the life that seems like a child's play is something I hate the most!" Kuroda-kun took a sip of beer and sighed.

"Alas! Is this the gift of the control system? We are hoping for the Athenian style of free system that gives us individual freedom when this kind of Spartan life is revived."

The night outside the window covered all the scenery of the fields and hills, only the sound of the wheels broke the silence of the universe.

The next day, at Osaka Station, when I turned my head and saw his posture standing blankly on the platform, it was as if infinite shadows and sorrows were piled up on his healthy shoulders.

Cursing 200

— TK

Under the Scorching Sun 201

— Tie Ming

(I)

A blue sky covers an endless green plain,

Not a shadow of a flying bird can be found in the fields;

The hot wind of the scorching heat tiresomely

Teases the grass and low treetops like a challenge.

In the six or seven-foot-tall cornfield,

Several tired and thin figures are working:

The brown soil stubbornly resists the hoe,

And the clumps of soil are as solid as stones.

Withered vines hang all over the sparse melon shed,

And the leaves of the wildflowers under the pergola are also bare.

Several skinny dogs are lying with their tongues out,

They silently guard the owner's thatched hut.

(II)

By the bank of the stagnant and turbid river,

People inhale the foul stench,

Trampling in the mud like machines.

A stack of straw is piled as high as the eaves,

Fearlessly reflecting the light of the scorching sun;

Several small trees hang down in frustration,

And some of the branches and leaves are as dry and yellow as rice stalks.

The working people are hunching their backs, panting,

They dare not look up at the sun;

Sweat drips from their bronze-colored skin,

Moistening every green seedling in the loosened soil.

Memories of a Small Person in a Tragic Scene 202

— Yu

Also Considered a Commemoration

It would be best to spend three years "facing the wall" or ten years in "seclusion." Perhaps then the blood could cool, and the senses could become numb. Even if one cannot become a detached high monk, one could at least become a disciple of a saint who endures insults. Holding up the pen, one could "dutifully acknowledge" everything. Putting down the pen, one could obediently be a good citizen. If society strips away all its material conditions, then what remains is merely man-made right and wrong, and a so-called good citizen is one who lives in that society without any sense of right or wrong. Saying "yes" and echoing "yes," saying "no" and echoing "no." If one says "yes" but thinks "no," then one's "seclusion" is not deep enough, and one's "sitting in meditation" is insufficient. One may still not be qualified to be a remnant of a prosperous age. How must one be? There is no specific standard. If one could follow the Way of Lao-tzu and Zhuang-tzu, and go even further by forgetting right and wrong, taking others' right and wrong as one's own, while one's own right and wrong are not involved, perhaps then one could succeed. However, you must lie in bed at midnight and think it over thoroughly. Can you do it? Can you, or can't you? There is no bargaining in between. If you want to bargain, that is "business." However, for people like us who are still not free from the smell of rice, and who consider ourselves to be someone of importance, it is not "business" to those who hold the "sacred right." The explanation that this is not "business" is that you are both "entertaining prostitutes and accommodating scholars," but you want to consider yourself superior to prostitutes and actors. Or perhaps the world no longer needs a "tongue," but you still want to go back and ask your wife, open your mouth, and solemnly ask her to see if your tongue still exists. Or see if your hand has been broken like Kong Yiji's, or whether the rope around your neck can continue writing. Mentioning that old pen, you are as happy as a beggar mentioning his staff, a blaze of joy. But when you write, you must consider "neighborly policies," and you must consider "one year two months," etc. Would you like to be like that son of the sea god in Greek mythology, "Proteus"? He possesses foresight and the power to change his appearance. If you have such power, you can move your tongue according to objective situations, and you can also change your appearance according to objective situations. Then it will work. Can it be done? If not, then refrain from speaking, or "talk about humor," or "tell ghost stories," or "drink bitter tea," or "take a sea bath," or "say the weather is nice today," or "play dead." However, today happens to be such a day, which is a difficult "knot" to untie. Then I thought of what the old Taoist Zhang Yaoxing in the legend of "The Peach Blossom Fan" said to the infatuated couple Hou Fangyu and Li Xiangjun during the memorial service for the Chongzhen Emperor: "Where is the country? Where is the home?" Now, like those Christians who say, "Blessed by God," we still have a home and a country, but thirty million people have no home and no country. Talk about humor? "Drink bitter tea?" "Go up a volcano?" "Take a sea bath?" "Say the weather is nice today?" "Play dead?" None of them seem appropriate. Then may I ask, what should we do? Let's hold off on answering these for a moment. Mentioning "The Peach Blossom Fan" reminded me of the storyteller Liu Jingting. So, when the review committee's day comes… let me act as a storyteller and you as the audience. I will gather old stories, and you can criticize them. But I don't have Liu Jingting's talent. Naturally, I can't tell stories as vividly as Ma Zai. At the same time, my gathering of old stories is not for the sake of lamenting, but to find some material for discussion from the old stories themselves, to address reality. However, cutting history from the side will make it a series of dead facts, and the interpretation of these facts can vary depending on one's position. But the evolution of history itself will negate all arbitrary interpretations. I am now discussing the great issue of historical truth, but I can't discuss such lofty principles, and you won't listen. I'd better act as a storyteller and fulfill the duties of a storyteller.

Not long ago, I remember that an old opera house in Shanghai performed "Hate of the Late Ming Dynasty." I have no affinity for Peking Opera, and I didn't have the courage to watch the scene where the big gongs and drums shook "heaven and earth." However, a few months ago, I went to "Coal Hill," the historical site where "Hate of the Late Ming Dynasty" was played out, twice. The protagonist in that scene, the Chongzhen Emperor, has long been buried in a corner of the Thirteen Tombs. The five pavilions arranged in a line on Coal Hill have also been freshly painted because the Beijing Municipal Government is renovating the city. The magnificent colors of the painted rafters and embroidered beams may be just like the gorgeous scenery on the Shanghai stage. When you enter such a realm and see such a scene, and if you are not guided by an old Beiping person, or have not received more than six years of education, and don't even know this period of history, or even don't have the good fortune of a Shanghainese to have the opportunity to see this "remnant of hatred" being performed, or even if you are on the scene but have not read books like the Beijing Guide, you will never believe that this place was the place of death for the emperor of that generation who was destined for tragedy. However, I had a preconceived notion in my mind. When I entered the gate to Coal Hill, I thought of that historical fragment, and there was already a tragic scene in my heart. So, when I walked up the stone steps leading to the mountain and saw the white pine forest on both sides of the road, the gray-white color of their trunks and branches felt terribly desolate, as if they were forever commemorating the remnant of this fallen country. The "Guilty Locust" below, on whose side branches Emperor Chongzhen hanged himself, its old trunk, hollow and split into two, unable to bear the weight of its sin, and the withered leaves dyed gray, and the solemn-faced black fence surrounding it, and the stele outside the wall with white stones and vermilion characters "Site where Emperor Ming Si Zong died for his country," were all enough to draw my attention from the real scene to the theatrical scene of historical tragedy. Emperor Ming Si Zong is still active in people's minds today, probably because he is a character in a tragedy. However, I am not now, like those "examiners" of the former Qing Dynasty, squeezing into the doghouse-like "examination hall" to be forced to write a treatise on Emperor Ming Si Zong. I don't need to comment on whether this last emperor was good or bad. I think his tragic death, as far as he himself is concerned, made him seem like a Han Chinese. That is enough. This point is already higher than the political failures of Emperor Huizong and Emperor Qinzong of the Song Dynasty, and political failures are nothing. If he had been born in modern times, he might have been able to take a plane and escape from Beiping, without suffering such a tragic fate. Perhaps, as Mr. Huang Zongxi, a remnant of the late Ming Dynasty, hoped in his "Mingyi Daifanglu," he could have been like Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang Dynasty during the An Lushan Rebellion, who fled to Sichuan, or Emperor Daizong during the Tubo Rebellion, who fled to Shaanxi, or Emperor Dezong during the Zhu Ci Rebellion, who fled to Fengtian, and eventually achieved the goal of restoration. Therefore, he believed that the fall of the Ming Dynasty was due to the miscalculation of establishing the capital in Beiping. Speaking of this issue, it just so happens to contradict the opinion of some modern people who believe that if the capital of the National Government were not in Nanjing, but still in Beiping, the situation in North China might not have been so. Speaking of this, I want to be like that shape-shifting "Proteus" again, to impersonate a political commentator and comment on the rights and wrongs. Of course, my views are not worth laughing at by those brilliant political commentators. But at least it represents a bit of my opinion. Fine, it is reasonable and proper to move the capital to avoid the enemy's sharp edge and seek restoration gradually. Taking other countries as examples, New Turkey did not make Constantinople its capital but moved its capital to Ankara, and New Russia did not make St. Petersburg its capital but moved its capital to Moscow. The purpose is nothing else but that those two places were too close to the imperialist forces and were easily surrounded. Therefore, the leaders of these two countries moved their capitals inland to avoid the deep blows of foreign forces on their emerging revolutionary forces. But at the same time, we must not forget that the political power of these two countries was able to stabilize, and the forces of imperialism were able to be repelled, because of the years of bloody battles fought by the people of these two countries. It was not that moving the capital and escaping the oppression of foreign forces could remove the shackles. If there had not been years of struggle, I believe that Lenin and Trotsky would have been either on the guillotine or made lifelong prisoners in Kamchatka. Where would there have been New Russia? Where would there have been the construction of the Five-Year Plan? And Kemal would certainly have been imprisoned by the Greeks on some desert island like Abd el-Krim, the Rif chieftain of Morocco. Where would there have been New Turkey? Therefore, those mechanical people who think that by establishing the capital in Beiping, the territory of North China can be preserved without resorting to armed resistance are, to put it disrespectfully, truly seeing ghosts in broad daylight. Although Beiping is surrounded by mountains and rivers, and has the danger of being a stronghold, because of its economic weakness, the constraints of the Boxer Protocol, and the fact that the railway network in the Northeast is under foreign control, warships can arrive in the morning and leave in the evening, and troops can be transported into Shanhaiguan within a few days. It is not necessary to mention Emperor Yingzong of the Ming Dynasty's "hunting at Tumubao" or Emperor Wuzong's "being trapped in Yanghe." The Qing Dynasty was captured by foreigners twice. At present, the three northeastern provinces have been lost, the six counties of Chahar have been lost, the pseudo-autonomous region of eastern Hebei has been formed, and the foreign garrison in Tianjin has been expanded. The ancient city, which has been the capital for nearly a thousand years, which many famous domestic scholars and scholars four years ago wanted to use the mercy of foreigners to close off as the so-called "cultural city," is now an isolated county, like a remaining fruit, in the hands of people, and will be picked off with just a wave of the hand. What is there to talk about the solidity of "golden walls and boiling moats"? Moreover, judging from historical precedents, losing Xulong, Hebei is a plain, with simply no danger to defend. However, readers, do not misunderstand. What I mean is not that we are willing to give up our territory, but that we should further restore our lost territory so that we have danger to defend. The current problem is not about bargaining, but about life and death. You see, what is constantly being lost is land, and what is constantly being put forward is conditions. From the Yalu River in the east to the Yin Mountains in the west, where is there a clean land? The masses of the Chinese nation, please do not forget the national crisis, please do not forget the past history. That brave soldier once stained the blood of Xifengkou. Our border poets once sang, "The border is full of Han, and the barbarian cavalry is driving south." That strategically important Juyongguan Pass, our poets also sang, "The Han family can use troops to open up exotic cities." The tomb of Zhaojun, who was rich in drama during her lifetime and still left a clod of earth after her death, our great realist poets also sang, "Once she went to the Zidai and connected to the northern Han, leaving only the green tomb facing the sunset." The historical facts woven from time and space, people and events are all our markers for driving out the soil. How to think of ways to preserve what is being lost, and how to think of ways to restore what has already been lost, are all things that every Chinese people should strive for.

— Editor

We all know that humans are the most intelligent of all creatures. Where does this intelligence ultimately reside? The brain's specific function is to control the distribution of spirit throughout the body. Nerves branch out from the brain, encircling the entire body. Five Years! 211

— Fang Kewen

The September 18th Incident, this day of bloody remembrance, is its fifth anniversary today. In these five years, what has become of our country? We need not say more; the stark facts are laid out before us. On this tragic anniversary, my emotions are too agitated, and I simply cannot think of what words to use to express what I want to say. (I think every compatriot, except those who willingly become slaves and accomplices of tigers, feels this way!) Furthermore, this blood debt will definitely not be settled simply by remembering it on the anniversary. "Drinking cold water in winter, every drop is remembered in the heart." We will definitely not forget the "cold water" in ordinary times, but on this tragic anniversary, it only further evokes the situation when we "drank cold water" and makes us think with shame: Oh, it has been a full five years!

Today, five years later, I do not want to say much. I just want to give a warning to my compatriots: The greatest "humiliation" ("humiliation" is not quite appropriate, because in reality this is a matter of "survival" for each of us, and cannot be summed up by such an abstract conceptual noun). We have "endured humiliation and carried heavy burdens" for five years. The "humiliation" of the past five years has not only not lessened but has also increased. Therefore, the focus of the problem now is not on how to wash away the "humiliation" of the past but on how to prevent the "humiliation" from increasing. Of course, we know and believe that this is a dual problem, and a solution cannot be achieved by solving it separately.

For this reason, I would just like to copy some recent news reports below to let us see what the situation is like today, five years later, and how it will develop.

To commemorate the fifth anniversary of the September 18th Incident and to encourage people to immigrate to Manchuria, the Japanese Army, the Colonial Affairs, Agriculture and Forestry Ministries, the "Manchukuo" Concord Association, the Manchurian Immigration Association, etc., are holding a grand Immigration Propaganda Week from yesterday to the 18th. Immigration lecture meetings are being held throughout the country. The General Staff Headquarters of the Army Ministry, the Agriculture and Forestry, Colonial Affairs, and Finance Ministries, the Manchurian Affairs Bureau, and the South Manchurian Railway Company have sent personnel to form ten lecture teams to tour and give lectures. At the same time, film screenings of the September 18th Incident and symposiums on the September 18th Incident are being held to promote militaristic thought and encourage people to invade foreign countries. Currently, local veterans associations, youth groups, and national defense women's associations are also actively engaged in propaganda. (Tokyo dispatch, 11th)

To commemorate the fifth anniversary of the September 18th Incident, the Japanese authorities are holding a general mobilization of outdoor exercises for students in Dalian on that day. Approximately 3,500 people will participate, starting at 5:30 am. The East and West armies will use China as a hypothetical enemy to perform a heroic attack. (Dalian dispatch, 14th)

This is about "commemoration," and we can already see how different things are. Let's set this aside and take a look at how others are "supporting" us to end this article.

On the evening of the 13th, several heavy trucks flying a certain country's flag, fully loaded with cotton yarn and carrying several people from that country, were driving on the Baojia Highway... The Japanese textile industry has recently been actively expanding its business in Tianjin. Previously, Kanegafuchi Spinning Co. purchased the Yuyuan and Huaxin yarn factories, and Toyo Spinning Co. purchased Yufeng, renovating the factory's interior and expanding its business. Now, Shanghai Spinning Co. also has plans to advance north... As a result of negotiations with the Chinese side, it has been decided to purchase 70,000 ping of land... It is said that the construction of the factory will begin next spring and will be completed by the end of the year. (Tianjin dispatch, 15th)

The number of Japanese inspecting North China has recently increased sharply. In the past, most went to China alone, but recently they have been organizing groups, especially inspection groups dispatched by various chambers of commerce and industry... (Tianjin dispatch, 15th)

Finally, I must add one more unnecessary comment, which is that due to space constraints, the news reports excerpted above are only some of the very brief ones seen in the newspapers. I would like to ask readers to go and read the others themselves. Fortunately, they are everywhere. Moreover, in the above, we can really "see the whole leopard through one spot."
