Long ago, he had this idea:

Get some money, take a photo, and send it to the distant home!

To this day, this idea has not been realized, which makes him very painful. He works as a errand boy in a usury company opened by an Indian boss. When the debtor's date arrives, regardless of winter or summer, near or far, he has to run to that house to collect the debt. Sometimes when he runs back, his legs are so sore and numb that they don't feel like his own. Too tired? His annual salary is only thirty yuan.

Thirty yuan, he has to supplement his shoes and socks, and he has to send money home. Where would he have the money to take a photo?

He is getting older with worry!

When he is down, he comes to me, opens the conversation box, stiffly, it is always the same old story: how good his hometown is, how obedient his wife is, he has no money to take a photo, he dreamed of that little thing again last night...

Perhaps after reciting that set, he will hum Qinqiang opera.

But these days, he hasn't sung Qinqiang opera for a long time. He is getting thinner, his face is like the sky in the yellow plum season, gloomy. And he doesn't talk much anymore, keeping his mouth closed all the time.

I am really worried that he will fall ill.

"Buddy! Let me tell you, I guess I'm having a lucky streak. Yesterday the boss suddenly called me over. Guess what's up?"

The day before yesterday, he came to me, his face much brighter, and after telling me these few words, he kept me in suspense.

"A bonus?"

"No, no!"

He smiled and denied it. Then he told me: He was told to collect a debt. The other party was a tough nut to crack and refused to pay after several attempts. This time, the boss lost his temper and told him to take care of this matter: if soft tactics don't work, use hard ones; if hard ones don't work, take him to the company. At any rate, he had to squeeze oil out of him this time. Finally, he said: Isn't it my lucky streak? The boss promised in person: If I get the money, I'll split it two-eight with me.

"This time you should be able to take a photo."

He chuckled and left.

Today I saw him in this room again.

Nothing has changed, still old, and the wrinkles on his face seem to be deeper, with a bruise around his eye.

"What's wrong, with your eye?"

I pointed to the corner of his left eye.

He coughed, with a sigh, and shook his head repeatedly:

"This, this was hit by that rascal. Damn it, that rascal, really fierce, didn't pay the money and even hit people! He hit my eye."

"What happened then?"

"Later, I and a buddy dragged him to the company."

"Then the boss must have given you a bonus."

As if my words had touched his sore spot, he stood up abruptly, and a furious light flashed in his small eyes.

"Damn it! That heartless bastard! I got hurt, and he said I was useless and fired me."

After a while, his anger turned into sorrow, and he suddenly sighed!

"When can I take a photo?"

Then he coughed again, his face flushed red, and the veins on his forehead bulged like earthworms.

In his series of coughs, I seemed to hear the groan of a dying man. (The End)

Small Vegetable Market 213

Harmful to Hygiene 214

— Ding Ni

Called Semi-Qualified Scholar wrote "Xinglong Restaurant" in three lines of regular script on three square-cut red papers, and just covered the faded "Daxing Restaurant" on the old signboard. Hang up four red cloth lanterns, the atmosphere of a new shop.

On a counter by the threshold, green stone jars are piled as high as small graves, all full, soy-stewed ribs, sprouted beans, steaming with different flavors? Directly drilling into people's noses. On the blue-and-white dishes, there are also several kinds of side dishes. A drunkard carrying five taels of dregs-burned wine, with two fingers as dirty as fire citrus, took some chili-fried shredded meat without meat, put it in his mouth and chewed for a while. It seemed not enough to play, so he took some more something and put it in his mouth and chewed. Only then did he take a plate of sprouted beans, which he seemed to have decided on long ago, and ran in.

"If there were a band of musicians, how lively it would be." Wang Boss, sitting on a high stool by the counter, thought so, and concealed the trace of a smile that he had just shown while looking at the four red lanterns. However, thinking that he had been working as a shop assistant for others for these years, and he actually had a day to start his own business and open a shop, he smiled again!

Huang Pang hit the iron pot loudly, without any melody. The waiter responded with a "Hey," and brought in the soup noodles that had been cooked on the stove. He put the lard into the red-hot empty pot and put in some raw materials and covered it. Then, he stretched out an arm, whose sweat hair had been burned off by the stove fire, and picked up a pot full of noodles, skillfully dividing it into coarse bowls that were smaller than basins placed on the stove, one bowl after another.

"Holding a pot full of noodles as if it's nothing, his arm is really strong. But, who was the bastard who gave him the nickname Huang Pang?" Boss Wang felt a little injustice for his capable stove clerk.

A group of customers taking it with them (Note 1) with coarse bowls of soup noodles were talking quietly and left cheaply. Then, another group of coarse bowls was brought up, shouting "Next bowl of soup noodles"!

Counting twenty-two coppers, and then counting twenty-two coppers. Boss Wang felt that the soup noodle business today was not bad. He suddenly wondered why his waiter, who was like a lark, was not so energetic. He turned around to see what the old man was doing? What was he doing? The lark was holding a teacup, slowly sipping tea. There were two customers in the hall, one was a drunkard that Boss Wang knew, and the other was eating soup noodles, sweating profusely. Boss Wang originally wanted to reprimand the waiter, but seeing the situation, he didn't say anything.

Why are there so few dine-in (Note 2) customers? Dim sum shops all rely on a lot of dine-in customers to make some money. Today's soup noodle business is a loss-making business! Boss Wang looked worriedly at the pile of coppers in the drawer, "Not even a dime has been seen for half a day. If this goes on, won't we have to close the door"?

He pondered hard, for a long time before he opened his eyelids. A plan to keep the shop open remained in his mind: "Bring his wife out from the countryside and let her manage the shop, and he would be the waiter himself, wouldn't that work"?

At this time, a person in a Western suit ran into the shop, followed by a person in a short shirt. Boss Wang thought they were big customers and was about to stand up to greet them. The person in the Western suit said loudly, "Boss, how about what I told you this morning"?

When Boss Wang saw that it was the garbage collector, he became anxious in his heart. But he immediately squeezed out a smile, "Please sit! Please sit! Waiter, pour tea!

"No need to be polite." The garbage collector didn't sit down, and put the tea handed over by the waiter aside: "How is it? Tell me"? Then, he pulled Boss Wang to the back door and said softly, "This is the rule, every new shop can't escape it, and..."

"But, sir, all my capital has been spent. Business is not good today, and I only earned four or five yuan..."

"Don't say it! If you say it like this, I still have to lend you some capital"? The garbage collector's tone became fierce: "What's it going to be"?

"Sir, there's really no way, I have to ask you to forgive me"!

"Hmph! You can't get the walnut meat out if you don't knock"! The garbage collector ran to the door: "Come! This braised chicken is already ruined. There are flies on that rib. It's unsanitary, pour it out."

The person following the garbage collector held two jars of things to pour out, Boss Wang wanted to stop him, but he was pushed away by the garbage collector. The two jars of things slammed into the dog-chewing bucket (Note 3).

"And the chimney hood above is not well made, which is harmful to hygiene. I'll give you a deadline to redo it tomorrow. If it's not done when I come to see it tomorrow, don't blame me!"

Two tears hung on the corner of Boss Wang's eyes, and he stared blankly at the dog-chewing bucket.

(Note 1) Taking it with them to buy.

(Note 2) Running to the shop to eat.

(Note 3) A bucket for holding the leftovers of the diners.

Duck 215

— Yun

The sun had already fallen into the mountains across the way, and a glow of sunset dyed the sky red. Wisps of black smoke were blowing out of the chimneys on every thatched roof. It was suppertime.

Granny Zhu, a widowed old woman, was holding a thin bamboo pole and standing by the river, "Hoo, hoo" driving the ducks into the pen. Those ducks were caught in the summer, and now they have grown red feet and shiny feathers, finding food for themselves in the small stream. Hearing Granny Zhu's "Hoo, hoo" sound, they lined up in a line, quacking, and walked ashore one after another. Following Granny Zhu's thin bamboo pole gently waved, like children knowing their own home, wobbling along the embankment.

Granny Zhu, like a military officer, stood at the end, still making "Hoo, hoo" sounds in her mouth. Passing Aunt Li's door, Aunt Li had just finished eating dinner with her son and wanted to move the table and stools back to the house to sleep.

"Granny, those ducks are growing up."

Aunt Li respected Granny Zhu the most, saying that she was a widowed old woman relying on spinning and weaving, raising chickens and ducks to make a living. Even a man probably didn't have her skills. Therefore, Aunt Li was the one who got along best with Granny in this pond. She often said to those pond people who looked down on the widowed old woman: It's also a hard life to be a widowed old woman. She doesn't break the law, doesn't rob or steal. Seeing how hard-working and diligent she is, if she were a man, she would probably be a great old man! Stop saying that you're unlucky to meet a widowed old woman, you can't even find such a widowed old woman with a lantern.

When Granny Zhu heard Aunt's Li's words, she immediately slowed down her pace and said, "Yes, thanks to the pond for having a lot of oil and water (fish, shrimp, etc.), and the snails are also cheap. If there was a duck plague like last year, this old woman's bones wouldn't have anywhere to bury!"

Saying that, Granny Zhu also laughed herself. She wasn't laughing that her words were too blunt, she was laughing that the group of ducks had gathered at her doorstep, quacking, they were waiting for a hearty dinner.

"Aunt, your Genfu likes to eat duck, I'll send one over in a few days."

"No, no! You raise them so hard, how can I be embarrassed to eat yours? Just let me have a small one, to satisfy A Gen's mouth."

Granny Zhu didn't listen to her, and hurried onto the pond embankment. A basket of snails had already been placed at her door, and the group of ducks were surrounding the basket, quacking. But Granny helped with this hearty dinner, the ducks didn't see it as easily as swallowing a small fish flipping over in the pond. Granny Zhu sat on the stool, first counting whether any were missing, then picked up the one closest to her, held its belly to see if it was full, and then opened its mouth to stuff as many snails as possible. Then she put it into the bamboo cage. The ducks were stuffed with snails, all swollen in their small necks, and then they quacked and fluttered in the cage, until those snails were sent into their stomachs, and then they comfortably waited in the cage for Granny to send them to the pen, like a person who had finished dinner.

One by one, stuffing snails, the sky was already completely dark without her realizing it. Granny Zhu stretched lazily from the stool, fumbled into the house in the dark, lit a torch (a simple light), went back out to carry the cage back to the pen, and then went to the door with peace of mind.

Page 21

She only cooked one meal for lunch and ate cold rice soaked in hot water in the evening. However, she was too tired, and sometimes she would lie down on the bed after serving the ducks, she needed rest more than eating.

Today she was very happy, the ducks had all grown up, and none of them had died. In a few days, the restaurants in the town would send someone to the pond to collect the ducks, and she could sell a lot of money. Those ducks had cost her a lot of effort to raise from catching them to this size. With this money, she could rest for a while in the autumn and then spin yarn in the winter. Thinking about it, she went to the duck pen again to inspect it, to see if the paper paste on the door was twisted, those hateful weasels often dragged away her ducks and chicks.

She didn't even want a little dish with the cold rice soaked in hot water, and she swallowed two bowls of rice quickly. With a happy heart, she went to bed. Perhaps Granny Zhu would have a happy dream tonight, dreaming that her son came back and she was no longer a widowed old woman.

Riverside 216

— Yago

——A Record of the Jin River——

The thick pillars trembled amidst the white poplars and reeds; a dull, gray mist began to permeate the Jin River. In the reeds, the wind flew past, disturbing flocks of wild ducks, which whirled in the air in alarm, only to disappear into another clump of reeds. Raindrops slanted onto the calm water surface, shuddering for a moment before turning into clusters of ripples, expanding and rippling. Dozens or hundreds of them collided, forming a small wave, which drifted far away with the wind, striking the hull of the boat and emitting a low, mournful sound.

The boatman, wearing a disgruntled expression, climbed into the cabin and said that the wind had picked up on the river and the rain was falling so heavily that they could no longer travel. They would have to wait for the wind and rain to pass before continuing. We thought about it: it was indeed dangerous to travel in a storm. Hadn't we seen a report in the newspaper just a few days ago about a hurricane heading towards the China Sea? So we agreed.

The boatman steered the boat to the shore, dropping anchor under a row of white poplar trees and mooring. After furling the sail, he climbed into the cabin, sat down, and began to smoke his small pipe.

The rain continued to patter, striking the thin iron sheet of the boat canopy and producing crisp sounds. We all lay quietly in our berths, listening to the sharp whistling of the wind and the sound of the rain, which powerfully absorbed our thoughts.

Gradually, the sound of the rain became more sparse and slow, but the wind continued to blow. The boatman tapped his pipe on the boat plank, knocked out the ashes, and extinguished the remaining sparks with his foot. He then silently climbed out, stood on the deck, turned back to us, and said in a low voice: "The rain is about to stop..."

He was silent, as if listening to something. Before long, his hands suddenly began to tremble, his face turned pale, and his mouth convulsed. He climbed into the cabin, looking at everyone with uneasy and bewildered eyes.

His sudden change of movement made me curious, so I questioned him. He frowned deeply and said in a worried tone:

"This is beyond our control, sir..." He then paused to think, tilting one ear and listening intently. We, too, seemed to be influenced and paid attention. A kind of noisy sound, faint and soft, was echoing in the distance, sometimes becoming so bright and clear, and sometimes quietly fading away.

"It's a kind of shouting..." the boatman murmured in a pained tone.

"And it sounds like it's coming from a woman's throat..." I added.

The boatman shrugged uneasily and climbed out again, standing quietly at the hatch. We followed as if drawn by something.

The rain had stopped, and fine raindrops were still drifting. The sky was very verdant, tinged with blue. On the deck, we cautiously followed the sound, searching in that direction; but we saw nothing.

"Over there, look..." The boatman turned back, pointing far away with his hand. We followed his gaze and, yes, over there, facing the Jin River, was a small village of seven or eight farmhouses arranged in a row. In front of the houses was a long threshing ground. The ground was empty and desolate, but at this moment, more than a dozen people in gray clothes were coming out of one of the houses in a single file. They were all disheveled, bareheaded, their faces flushed red. Some held a chicken in their hands (which often struggled, flapping its wings and crying mournfully); others were still waving a bayonet in the air menacingly. They staggered and bumped into each other as if drunk. On the other side, three people were pumping their short legs, chasing a young and thin woman. Her hair and long skirt fluttered high in the air, and she emitted rapid and hurried cries, running around the threshing ground and dashing through the fields...

"They are chasing that woman..." the boatman said in a distressed tone, with a hint of despair.

"Who are they?" I asked, puzzled.

"The XX Volunteer Corps stationed in the nearby village... There's a large detachment in Huangtang, and a small detachment in Jiujiaowan, this one belongs to Huangtang. Here, they often run into farmhouses for no reason, stealing everything they can see and get, and some go after young women..." After saying this, he looked up at the azure sky with a worried expression, muttering: "The rain has stopped, let's go!..."

Looking up, the rain threads were gone, and a cluster of sunlight was shining in the clouds.

Loneliness 217

— Shen Jiaqian

After throwing the third cigarette butt into the spittoon, the clock held in the goddess's hand struck ten times like a lark. I rubbed my hands and felt that I should say goodbye to the host.

The hostess had just stood up from the sofa next to the host. She yawned, perhaps wanting to go to the back room, but seeing that I had picked up my hat and was about to leave, she returned to the sofa and said before I could:

"Mr. X, won't you sit a little longer?" Her eyes rolled as she glanced at the goddess holding the clock. "It's ten o'clock already. — Do you have some kind of meeting?"

She tilted her head and rolled onto the back of the sofa where her husband was sitting, laughing playfully.

"Nothing going on, right?" her husband asked me seriously. "It's raining heavily outside."

He handed me a cigarette.

There was nothing going on, I just thought about finding this young couple to escape a lonely evening. Speaking of which, the evenings in Shanghai are not lonely at all, on the contrary, they are just the beginning of the fun? On the one hand, I am indeed too poor to afford to buy women's smiles, or go to the theater to listen to plays that I don't understand, and everywhere else shows that the evenings in Shanghai are not lonely. Then, it is lively enough in my apartment, with the singing of street girls downstairs, the comrades playing mahjong in the next room making a racket, and the women who come to each door to solicit business, often causing laughter and applause... The whole apartment is lively, it is a corner of Shanghai — no, it is exactly the prototype of Shanghai! However, my heart is lonely, and I feel that the evenings in Shanghai are too lonely.

Walking out of the apartment door, a few raindrops were already falling from the sky. I lowered my head, walking along the desolate road, following my own shadow. As the noisy sounds gradually faded away, I felt refreshed and wanted to do something. — Actually, this is not accurate, every day there are many things piled up in my head, and I need to finish them quickly, because a new lot of things will pile up in my head the next day. But I always let them pile up, pile up, until my brain swells with pain; finally, when I really want to do something, I can't sort things out clearly. So, I hesitate again, increasing [the pile], and I no longer have the desire to do anything. Therefore, what I am talking about now, wanting to do something, is very, very small in scope, like finding a friend to chat with. Thinking like this, when I passed my friend's house, I did not hesitate to ring his doorbell.

He was an old classmate from our middle school. In school, our relationship was very good, because we both participated in the parade of the Nanjing Road blood incident, and we were both arrested. We held hands tightly in the detention center, smiling silently at each other. But after graduation, we went down two different paths. He went to university, and after graduating, he married a young and beautiful wife. With the help of his wealthy father, he used the loan to become a compradore, which is naturally a very comfortable occupation. I did not advance to university, and the jobs I found were all short-term, and unemployment often gripped me like a snake that would not let go. Although I was one of the guests at his wedding, with my poor appearance I no longer had the courage to visit him in his new home. Today, I didn't seem to be thinking about these things.

After the servant went in to inform him, my friend came out to greet me himself, shaking my hand tightly, just like before. He invited me upstairs to his bedroom, introduced me to his newlywed wife, and said with a smile: "You've come at the right time, we're too lonely. Listen, at night, this place is like a deserted temple, although there's a radio in the east and a radio in the west, these things are the most annoying."

He finished speaking in one breath and then added, "Come and chat often when you have time."

I smiled and accepted the cigarette handed to me by his wife. Sitting on the soft sofa, I looked around this luxurious bedroom and thought, could they also feel lonely? It is true that this place is like a deserted temple, there are special signs on the roads in the residential area that prohibit honking car horns, but can't they use money to buy the liveliness of Shanghai? They don't seem to belong to the lonely group.

Talking, my friend revealed the reason for his loneliness.

"It's really tiring to live in Shanghai, dance halls, movie theaters... it's always the same. At night, it's like there's no place to put this body. Staying at home..."

He shook his head, not saying anything, probably because it would be too wasteful of this good evening, so he welcomed me to chat. But our loneliness is the same, but our paths are different, neither of us can solve this difficult problem for the other, or perhaps after talking more, it will increase each other's loneliness. After taking the fourth cigarette he handed me, I stood up to say goodbye.

"I've disturbed you a lot, you should go to sleep too."

His wife pouted at me, as if she guessed that I had some kind of appointment, wasn't it raining heavily outside?

"I wouldn't keep you if you had something to do." My friend shook my hand tightly, just like before. "Come and chat when you have time, I'm home more often in the evenings."

It was raining heavily outside, and because it was a residential area, no rickshaws passed by. I walked in the rain, letting the large raindrops hit my face, hands, and body. Perhaps this rain could relieve some of my loneliness.

All Shanghai Broadcasting Stations Suspend Entertainment Programs Today to Commemorate September 18th

Introduction 218

September 18th

XX inflicts poisonous calamity on China. Such a great provincial capital is ruined overnight. The three words become a timeless regret. Ten thousand people share a hundred years of shame. Thinking of the day when this turmoil began. Unknowingly, time flies and five autumns have passed. The years pass easily like flowing water. When will this endless hatred cease? The righteous army unfortunately suffered dispersal. Alas, the heroes' aspirations have not been fulfilled. The traces of villages and mounds are still there. The Yellow Dragon has not been slaked, and the regret is lingering. Alas, the blood of ten thousand men. Is exchanged for a few earthen mounds. Truly, the cold moon and dusk are when foxes and rabbits weep. A bleak wind and bitter rain lament the desolate mound. Fearing that the past will become a relic. Dare to use this writing to awaken sleeping gulls. Stop hesitating. Stop idling. The strong neighbor may not be willing to retract his ambitions.

Page 22

Page 23

May our compatriots cherish their hearts, love the country, and make strong efforts. With the ambition to turn the tide and avenge the great enemy. Lying on firewood and tasting gall must be remembered. By no means should we deceive others with superficial gestures. Empty words entrusted to the wind have no practical effect. Five minutes of enthusiasm brings shame. From now on, do not tread the original path again. Moreover, do not be in a prosperous place with no foresight. I only hope that the Han flag will be hung on the three borders soon. Let the barbarian horses not linger for long. Eliminate national humiliation and secure our homes. Then we can share wine and dispel all the sorrows of the ages. If we can achieve the hegemony of peace in one fell swoop. Our mighty name will shake other continents. May the Republic of China last forever. (Mimi Some Bottle Published Number)

There is courage;

There is decisiveness;

Like men,

You are not weak at all,

As strong as iron!

You have identified the goal,

And stride forward on the path of life illuminated by the sun,

The thickets and thorns,

The hideous and terrifying demons,

The fierce tigers, leopards, and wolves,

Cannot make you feel difficult or frightened!

Although: you have failed time and time again,

But; you are not disappointed:

Nor upset,

And even more determined to hold the fearless spirit of great sacrifice,

Forever, forever,

Fight against the dark forces,

Resist the demons of humanity!

Fight!

Resist!

For the sake of winning the sacred light of women's freedom!

"Life and Death Together" Protagonist - Chen Boer 222

— Photo by Du Ao
